فصل في بيان الحال
وأما بيانُ الحال:
فصل في بيان الحال:
فمثاله: فيما إذا رأى صاحب الشرع أمراً مُعاينةً فلم ينه عن ذلك كان سكوته بمنزلة صاحب الشرع
البيان أنه مشروع. والشفيع إذا عَلِمَ بالبيع وسَكَتَ كان ذلك بمنزلة البيان بأنه راض بذلك. والبكر إذا علمت بتزويج الولي، وسكتت عن الردّ كان ذلك بمنزلة البيان بالرضا السكوت والإذن، والمولى إذا رأى عبده يبيعُ ويشتري في السوق فسكت كان ذلك بمنزلة سكوت المولى الإذن، فيصير مأذوناً في التجارات.
إذا رأى صاحب إلخ: مثل ما رأى من مبايعات ومعاملات كان الناس يتعاملونها فيما بينهم، وماكل ومشارب كانوا يباشرونها فأقرهم عليها و لم ينكر عليهم، فدل سكوته أن جميعها مباح في الشرع؛ إذ لا يجوز من النبي عليه أن أقر الناس على محظور؛ إذ ليس من شأنه عليه أن يترك الناس على أمر منكر وقبيح، وقد قال الله تعالى في حقه: يأمرهم بالمعروف وينهاهم عن المنكر، وأيضاً قال: ﴿وَمَا يَنْطِقُ عَنِ الْهَوَى إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا وَحْيٌ يُوحَى الآية كذا في بعض كتب الأصول.
أنه مشروع إلخ : إذا البيان واجب عند الحاجة إلى البيان، فلو كان الحكم خلافه بين ذلك ولو بينه ليظهر، مثاله: إذا فعل عند النبيء عليه فعلاً فسكت كان سكوته دليلاً على مشروعية ذلك الفعل؛ لأنه لا يحل له السكوت إذا شاهد المحظور؛ لأن الساكت عن الحق شيطان، ولأنه بعث داعياً للخلق إلى الحق، فلما سكت كان سكوته دليلاً على مشروعيته كذا في "المعدن".
كان ذلك إلخ لأن لها عند تزويج الولي كلامين "نعم" و"لا" والحياء يحول بينها وبين "نعم" باختيارها الأزواج، ولا يحول بينها وبين "لا"؛ لعدم كثرة الحياء في الإنكار، فلو لم تكن راضية لأنكرت، فكان سكوتها دليلاً على الرضاء. فيصير مأذوناً إلخ: أي الضرورة دفع الغرور عمن يعامله، فإن الناس يستدلون بسكوته على إذنه ويتعاملون، فلو لم يجعل ذلك إذناً لكان سكوته غروراً في حقهم، وهو إضرابهم، وهما مدفوعان بالنص قال عليه: =
والمدعى عليه إذا نكل في مجلس القضاء يكون الامتناع بمنزلة الرضاء بلزوم المال
بطريق الإقرار عندهما، أو بطريق البذل عند أبي حنيفة به. فالحاصل أن السكوت في موضع الحاجة إلى البيان بمنزلة البيان.
وبهذا الطريق قلنا: الإجماعُ ينعقد بنص البعض وسكوت الباقين.
"لعن الله من ضر مسلماً أو غيره"، وقال عليه: "من غرنا فليس منا"، وقال الشافعي له: لا يكون ذلك إذناً؛ لأن سكوته عن النهي محتمل؛ لأنه قد يكون للرضا بتصرفه، وقد يكون لفرط الغيظ والنفرة، والمحتمل لا يكون حجة، ولنا أنه لو لم يجعل سكوته إذناً لأدى إلى الغرور والضرر، ودفعهما واجب بالنص كذا في "المعدن". إذا نكل: أي امتنع عن اليمين بعد استحلافه بعد. بمنزلة الرضاء لأنه لما سكت عن دفع دعوى المال في اليمين والقدرة عليه كان ذلك دليلاً على الرضاء بلزوم المال، وهذا بالاتفاق، لكنه اختلف في أنه بطريق الإقرار أو بطريق البذل، فالأول قولهما، والثاني قول أبي حنيفة لله كما قال المصنف، ولهذا المعنى لا يجري عنده الاستخلاف في الأشياء الستة، وعندهما يجري؛ لأن البذل لا يجري في هذه الأشياء، حتى لو قالت امرأة الرجل في دعوى النكاح عليهما: "لا نكاح بيني وبينك، ولكن بذلت نفسي" لا يعمل بذلها، وأما الإقرار فيعمل في هذه الأشياء كذا قيل.
بطريق البذل الإقرار لأن الامتناع كما يدل على الاحتراز عن اليمين الكاذبة يدل على الاحتراز عن نفس اليمين. في موضع الحاجة إنما قيد بقوله: "في موضع الحاجة؛ لأن السكوت في غير موضع الحاجة ليس بياناً، حتى أن صاحب الشرع إذا ذكر حكماً وسكت عن غيره وليس هناك حاجة داعية إلى البيان لا يدل على البيان، كقوله علي: اقطعوا السارق، واقتلوا القاتل" لا يدل على اسقاط الغرم وكفارة القتل؛ لأنه ليس هناك حاجة، فيجوز أن يكون قد بين القطع والقصاص بهذا، والغرم والكفارة بخبر آخر، أو فوضه إلى اجتهاد المجتهدين؛ لأنه لا يجب عليه بيان الأحكام دفعة واحدة، ولعله سكت ليبينه عنه وقت السوال وعند الحاجة إليه، فسكوته في غير وقت الحاجة إلى البيان لا يكون بياناً كذا في بعض الشروح. بمنزلة البيان: لأن البيان واجب عند الحاجة، فلو كان الحكم بخلافه لبين ذلك لا محالة؛ لأن الساكت عن الحق شيطان أخرس فجعل سكوته بياناً البتة. ينعقد إلخ وذلك إن وقعت حادثة فتكلم فيها بعض العلماء من الصحابة وغيرهم وسكت الباقون بعد بلوغهم الخبر ولا يردون ذلك عليهم بعد مضي مدة التأمل، والنظر في الحادثة، ثلاثة أيام، ويسمى هذا إجماعاً سكوتياً، وكذا إذا فعل واحد من أهل الإجماع فعلاً وعلم به أهل زمان و لم ينكر -
Chapter on Clarifying the Status. As for clarifying the status: Examples: When the Lawgiver observed something directly and did not forbid it, His silence is equivalent to a statement that it is legislated. The pre-emptor (shafi‘) when he learns of a sale and remains silent, that is equivalent to a statement that he is satisfied. The virgin when she knows of her guardian’s marriage and remains silent without rejection, that is equivalent to a statement of consent. The master when he sees his slave buying and selling in the market and remains silent, that is equivalent to permission, so the slave becomes authorized in transactions. Regarding “when the Lawgiver observed” etc.: For example, the transactions and dealings that people practiced among themselves, and the foods and drinks they consumed, He confirmed them and did not disapprove. His silence indicates that all are permissible in the Shari‘ah; it is not permissible for the Prophet (peace be upon him) to confirm people upon something prohibited, nor is it his nature to leave people upon something objectionable and evil. Allah the Exalted said regarding him: “He commands them to good and forbids them from evil” (Quran 7:157). Also He said: “And he does not speak from desire, it is only revelation revealed” (Quran 53:3-4). Thus in some books of Usul. “It is legislated” etc.: Explanation: Clarification is obligatory when needed; if the ruling were otherwise, he would have clarified it. His silence is evidence of the permissibility of that action because it is not lawful for him to remain silent when witnessing something prohibited; the silent one about the truth is a devil, and he was sent as a caller to the truth. Therefore his silence is evidence of its permissibility. This is from al-Ma‘din. “That is equivalent” etc.: Because the virgin when her guardian marries her has two statements: “yes” and “no”. Shyness prevents her from saying “yes” regarding her choice of spouse, but it does not prevent her from saying “no” because shyness is less in objection. If she were not consenting, she would object, so her silence is evidence of consent. “So he becomes authorized” etc.: Necessity requires preventing deception of those who deal with him; people infer his permission from his silence and deal with him. If that were not considered permission, his silence would be deception towards them, and that is deception and harm, both of which are prohibited by texts. The Prophet said: “May Allah curse the one who harms a Muslim or others.” He also said: “Whoever cheats us is not of us.” Al-Shafi‘i argued that it is not permission because his silence about prohibition is ambiguous; it could be due to consent or due to extreme anger and aversion, and the ambiguous cannot be evidence. Our proof: if his silence were not considered permission, it would lead to deception and harm, and removing these is obligatory by text. This is from al-Ma‘din. “If he refrains” (nukul): meaning he abstains from taking the oath after being asked to swear. This abstention is equivalent to consent to liability for the money, because he remained silent about rejecting the claim despite being able to do so, which is evidence of consent to liability. This is agreed, but there is a difference as to whether it is by way of admission (iqrar) or by way of offer (badhl). The first is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the second is the view of Abu Hanifa. This is why, according to him, (the procedure of) swearing does not apply to the six things, but according to them it does; because offer does not apply to these things. Even if a woman says to a man in a marriage claim: “There is no marriage between us, but I offer myself,” her offer is not valid, whereas admission is valid in these things. Regarding “by way of offer or admission”: Because abstention indicates avoidance of false oath as well as avoidance of the oath itself. The restriction “in a place of need” is because silence in a place without need is not a statement. If the Lawgiver mentions a ruling and remains silent about others where there is no need for clarification, it does not indicate anything. For example, “Cut off the hand of the thief, kill the killer” does not indicate exemption from compensation and expiation for killing, because there is no need for that. It is possible that He stated the cutting and retaliation by this text, and the compensation and expiation through another report, or He left it to the ijtihad of the mujtahids. It is not obligatory for Him to clarify all rulings at once; perhaps He remained silent to clarify later when needed. So silence in a time when clarification is not needed is not a statement. “Equivalent to statement”: Because clarification is obligatory when needed, so if the ruling were otherwise, He would have clarified it; the silent one about the truth is a mute devil. Therefore, His silence is considered a statement. “Ijmā‘ is established” etc.: This occurs when an incident occurs, some scholars from the Companions and others speak about it, and the rest remain silent after hearing the report, and do not reject it after a period of reflection and consideration of the incident – three days. This is called silent consensus. Similarly, if one of the people of consensus performs an action and the people of the time know about it and do not disapprove...
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi explains the important usul principle: 'Silence in a context where clarification is needed is equivalent to a statement.' The author begins by providing examples from the Prophet's practice. When the Prophet saw people engaging in transactions or eating certain foods and did not forbid them, his silence is evidence that such actions are permissible. This is because the Prophet is obligated to command good and forbid evil; he cannot remain silent upon seeing something prohibited. The same principle applies to the shafi‘ (pre-emptor) who knows of a sale and remains silent: his silence indicates consent. Similarly, a virgin who knows her guardian has arranged a marriage and does not object is deemed to have consented, since shyness prevents her from saying 'yes' but not from saying 'no'. Likewise, a master who sees his slave trading in the market and stays silent is considered to have given permission, thereby making the slave an authorized agent in business. The reasoning is that if silence were not taken as permission, it would lead to deception and harm to those who deal with the slave, and the texts prohibit deception and harm. The passage then discusses a dispute: Imam al-Shafi‘i argued that silence cannot be considered permission because it is ambiguous—it may indicate consent or extreme anger. However, the Hanafis maintain that because clarification is necessary in such contexts, silence must be interpreted as consent; otherwise, it would cause harm. The text also addresses the case of a defendant who refuses to take an oath (nukūl). All agree that the refusal is equivalent to accepting liability, but there is a difference whether it is by way of admission (iqrār) or by way of offer (badhl). Abu Hanifa holds it is an offer, which is why, according to him, the procedure of swearing does not apply to six specific things. Finally, the passage restricts the principle: silence is only considered a statement when there is a need for clarification. If there is no such need, silence does not imply anything. For example, the Prophet saying 'Cut off the hand of the thief' does not imply that one is exempt from compensation, because there is no need to clarify that at that moment. The passage ends by linking this principle to the concept of silent consensus (ijmā‘ sukūtī): when some scholars express an opinion and others remain silent after sufficient time for reflection, that silence is considered consent, thus forming consensus.

Key Terms
السكوت (al-sukūt): Silence in a context where clarification is needed is legally considered as a statement of consent or permissibility.
الرضا (al-riḍā): Consent, which can be inferred from silence in certain contexts such as marriage and sale.
الإذن (al-idhn): Permission, inferred from the master's silence when his slave trades in the market.
الإقرار (al-iqrār): Admission, one of the two interpretations for the defendant's refusal to take the oath (nukūl) according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
البذل (al-badhl): Offer/undertaking, the interpretation of nukūl according to Abu Hanifa, meaning the defendant offers to pay the claimed amount.
الإجماع السكوتي (al-ijmāʿ al-sukūtī): Consensus formed by some scholars expressing an opinion and others remaining silent after the report reaches them and after a period of reflection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does silence constitute a statement according to Hanafi usul, as explained in the passage?
A) Silence always indicates consent.
B) Silence when there is a need for clarification is evidence of consent.
C) Silence only indicates consent in financial transactions.
D) Silence never constitutes a statement.

Key Takeaway
Silence in a context requiring clarification is legally binding as a statement—this principle underpins the Prophet's tacit approvals, consent in marriage, permission in agency, and even silent consensus.

Al-Sunnah as Source

Definition and Categories of Sunnah in Usul al-Fiqh
Defines Sunnah linguistically and terminologically as the Prophet's utterances, actions, and approvals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Sunnah in its usul al-fiqh context, identify its three categories (qawl, fi'l, taqrir), and distinguish it from the Quran and from the furu' usage.

Core Idea
Sunnah in usul al-fiqh is the Prophet's every word, action, and silent approval—excluding the Quran—forming the second source of Islamic law.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi establishes the foundational definition of Sunnah as a source of law. Understanding this definition is crucial because it determines which prophetic reports are admissible as evidence. The passage also clarifies that the term 'sunnah' can have different meanings in different disciplines, and here it refers specifically to the body of prophetic traditions that serve as legal proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic definition
Start by noting that linguistically, 'sunnah' means a path or custom (طريقة وعادة). This broad meaning is the basis for the technical usage.
2
Identify the technical definition in usul
In usul al-fiqh, 'sunnah' refers specifically to what issued from the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) other than the Quran. This includes his speech (qawl), actions (fi'l), and tacit approvals (taqrir).
The passage explicitly excludes the Quran from this definition.
3
List the three components
Memorize the three categories: 1) Qawl (speech) – the Prophet's sayings, also called hadith; 2) Fi'l (action) – his actions; 3) Taqrir (tacit approval) – his silence upon witnessing something, indicating approval.
Taqrir is a key concept: silence does not necessarily mean disagreement; in legal terms it implies consent.
4
Note the exclusion
The definition explicitly excludes the Quran. The Quran is a separate source. Also excluded are actions or words of the Companions (sahaba) unless traced back to the Prophet.
5
Understand the quantity phrase
The passage says Sunnah is 'more than the number of sand and pebbles' – emphasizing its vastness. This highlights the importance of systematic principles to handle such a large body of evidence.
This is not a precise count but a rhetorical device to stress abundance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البحث الثاني في سنة رسول الله
وهي أكثر من عدد الرمل والحصى.
سنة:
هي في اللغة: الطريقة والعادة، وفي الاصطلاح العبادات النافلة ،والأدلة والمراد ههنا ما صدر عن النبي
غير القرآن من قول، ويسمى الحديث، أو فعل أو تقرير أي سكوت عند أمر يعاينه كذا في 'التلويح'.
The Second Research on the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah. And it is more than the number of sand and pebbles. Sunnah: In language: the path and custom. In terminology: the supererogatory acts of worship, and the evidences. What is intended here is what issued from the Prophet other than the Quran: from speech, and it is called hadith, or action, or tacit approval, i.e., silence regarding a matter he witnessed, as in 'al-Talwih'.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage introduces the second major source of Islamic law: the Sunnah of the Prophet (peace be upon him). It first emphasizes the vast quantity of Sunnah by comparing it to the uncountable grains of sand and pebbles. Then it provides two definitions: linguistically, 'sunnah' means a path or custom. In Islamic legal terminology, the word has multiple uses; here it means what is known as 'hadith' – the prophetic traditions. The passage specifies that the Sunnah consists of three components: the Prophet's words (qawl), actions (fi'l), and tacit approvals (taqrir/ikrar), which is his silence upon witnessing something. This definition excludes the Quran itself. The commentary notes that in other contexts, 'sunnah' can refer specifically to supererogatory acts of worship, but in usul al-fiqh, it refers to all prophetic reports that serve as evidence for legal rulings.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): What issued from the Prophet other than the Quran: speech (hadith), action, or tacit approval
التقرير (al-taqrir): The Prophet's silence upon witnessing something, indicating approval

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The Prophet's sayings (hadith)
B) The Prophet's actions
C) The Quran itself
D) The Prophet's silent approvals

Key Takeaway
Sunnah in usul al-fiqh is the Prophet's qawl, fi'l, and taqrir, excluding the Quran, serving as the second primary source of Islamic law.

The Three Categories of Khabar: Mutawatir, Mashhur, Ahad
Explaining the rationale for categorizing khabar and defining the three types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three categories of khabar (mutawatir, mashhur, ahad) based on their epistemological certainty and explain why the Sunnah is like the Quran in authority but varies in transmission.

Core Idea
Not all Prophet’s reports are equally certain; khabar is divided by transmission strength into mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad.

The Prophet’s speech (hadith) carries the same binding authority as the Quran, as confirmed by several Quranic verses. However, unlike the Quran which is transmitted with absolute certainty, the transmission of hadith can vary in reliability. This is why scholars categorize transmitted reports (khabar) into three levels: mutawatir (certain), mashhur (near-certain), and ahad (speculative). This lesson unpacks that tripartite division and its epistemological implications for legal derivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basis of Sunnah’s authority
Locate the Quranic verses cited in the passage that establish the Prophet’s speech as divinely guided and binding. Understand that these verses make the Sunnah equal to the Quran in requiring knowledge and action.
Key verses: 53:3, 59:7, 4:80.
2
Recognize the problem of transmission
Note the phrase: 'الشبهة في باب الخبر في ثبوته من رسول الله، واتصاله به' — the ambiguity lies in whether a report is authentically from the Prophet and connected to him. This is why categorization is needed.
Unlike the Quran, which is mass-transmitted, hadith transmission can be uncertain.
3
Define each category
From the passage, list the three categories: mutawatir (no ambiguity), mashhur (light ambiguity), ahad (probability and ambiguity). Understand the level of certainty each provides.
Mutawatir: certain (qat'i). Mashhur: near-certain (zann ghalib). Ahad: speculative (zann).
4
Connect categories to legal application
Understand that the category of a hadith determines whether its ruling is binding as certain knowledge or requires further verification before action. This is a core usul principle.
In Hanafi usul, only mutawatir and mashhur can establish 'ilm (certain knowledge); ahad establishes zann.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أقسام الخبر

خبر رسول الله بمنزلة الكتاب في حق لزوم العلم والعمل به، فإن من أطاعه فقد أطاع الله فما مرّ ذكره من بحث الخاص والعام والمشترك، والمجمل في الكتاب فهو كذلك في حق السنّة، إلا أن الشبهة في باب الخبر في ثبوته من رسول الله، واتصاله به، ولهذا المعنى صار الخبر على ثلاثة أقسام:

1 - قسم صح من رسول الله، وثبت منه بلا شبهة وهو "المتواتر".
2 - وقسم فيه ضرب شبهة وهو "المشهور".
3 - وقسم فيه احتمال وشبهة وهو "الآحاد".

الخبر: إنما اختار لغة الخبر ههنا دون السنة؛ لأن الأقسام من الخاص أو العام وغيرهما إنما يتأتى في القول دون الفعل. بمنزلة الكتاب: لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا يَنْطِقُ عَنِ الْهَوَى إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا وَحْيٌ يُوحَى﴾، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا آتَاكُمُ الرَّسُولُ فَخُذُوهُ وَمَا نَهَاكُمْ عَنْهُ فَانْتَهُوا﴾، وقوله تعالى: ﴿مَنْ يُطِعِ الرَّسُولَ فَقَدْ أَطَاعَ اللَّهَ﴾ وغير ذلك من النصوص والأخبار مما لا تعد ولا تحصى ويجري في الحديث جميع أقسام الكتاب مما سبق، إلا أنه لم يجر فيه، وذلك للاستغناء بذكره في بحث الكتاب كذا في "الحصول". فهو كذلك: أي البحث المذكور بتمامه يأتي في قسم السنة؛ لأن قوله حجة مثل الكتاب، وهو كلام مستجمع لوجوه الفصاحة والبلاغة، فتجري فيه هذه الأقسام أيضاً. إلا أن الشبهة: جواب سوال مقدر، وهو: أن السنة فرع الكتاب في بيان تلك الأقسام بأحكامها، فلا حاجة إلى عقد باب السنة برأسها، والجواب: بأن الاشتغال بذلك لفائدة تحتاج إليها، وهي بيان اتصال السنة بالنبي، فإنه فيه غموض لابد من انكشافه ولم يحصل إلا بما قال فيما بعد. باب الخبر إلخ جواب سوال مقدر، وهو: أنه إذا كان خبر رسول الله بمنزلة الكتاب ينبغي أن يكون كل خبره علي متواتراً قطعياً كالكتاب، فكيف صار الخبر ثلاثة أقسام كذا قيل .. ضرب شبهة إلخ : أي نوع خفيف من نوعها فالتنوين للتحقير، وكذا إضافة الضرب إليها أي: ليس فيه شبهة من كل وجه وقوله فيه احتمال وشبهة أي فيه احتمال قوي لصلوحه الصدق والكذب أي: فيه تجويز جانب [؟]
Chapter on the Categories of Khabar. The report of the Messenger of Allah is like the Book in terms of the necessity of knowledge and action upon it, for he who obeys him has obeyed Allah. So whatever has passed of discussion of specific, general, common, and ambiguous in the Book, so too in the Sunnah. However, the ambiguity in the chapter of khabar lies in its establishment from the Messenger of Allah and its connection to him. For this reason, khabar became three categories: 1. A category that is authentic from the Messenger of Allah and established from him without ambiguity, which is 'mutawatir'. 2. A category in which there is a kind of ambiguity, which is 'mashhur'. 3. A category in which there is probability and ambiguity, which is 'ahad'. [Commentary:] Khabar: He chose the term khabar here instead of sunnah because the categories of specific and general etc. only apply to speech, not action. 'Like the Book': due to His statement: {Nor does he speak from [his own] inclination} (53:3), and His statement: {And whatever the Messenger gives you, take it} (59:7), and His statement: {Whoever obeys the Messenger has obeyed Allah} (4:80), and other texts and reports beyond count. And all the categories of the Book apply to hadith as well, except that they are not applied here because it is sufficient to mention them in the discussion of the Book, as in 'al-Husul'. 'So too': i.e. the mentioned discussion in its entirety applies to the category of Sunnah, because his speech is a proof like the Book, and it is speech that combines all aspects of eloquence and rhetoric, so these categories also apply to it. 'Except the ambiguity': answer to a hypothetical question: that the Sunnah is a branch of the Book in explaining those categories with their rulings, so there is no need to dedicate a chapter for the Sunnah on its own. The answer: that the engagement with that is for a benefit that is needed, which is explaining the connection of the Sunnah to the Prophet, for it has a subtlety that must be uncovered, and it is not achieved except by what he says afterwards. 'Chapter of khabar etc.': answer to a hypothetical question: that if the report of the Messenger is like the Book, then every report of his should be mutawatir and certain like the Book, so how did khabar become three categories? So it was said... 'kind of ambiguity etc.': i.e. a light type of it, so the tanwin is for belittlement, and similarly the addition of 'kind' to it, i.e. it does not have ambiguity from every aspect. And his saying 'probability and ambiguity' i.e. in it there is a strong probability that it can be true or false, i.e. in it there is weighing of a side [?]
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a chapter ('Fasl') on the categories of transmitted reports (akhbar). The author explains that the Prophet's reports (hadith) are equivalent to the Quran in terms of being binding for knowledge and action, citing Quranic verses that establish the authority of the Prophet. However, unlike the Quran which is absolutely certain in its transmission, the transmission of the Prophet's reports can vary in certainty. Therefore, khabar is divided into three categories based on the strength of transmission. Mutawatir: reported by such a large number at every level that collusion on falsehood is impossible; it yields certain knowledge. Mashhur: reported from the Prophet by one or two companions but later became widely transmitted among the Salaf; it yields near-certainty but may require action. Ahad: reported by a smaller number, not reaching the level of tawatur; it yields speculative knowledge and is subject to further conditions. The commentary also addresses why the author uses 'khabar' instead of 'sunnah': because categories like 'amm' and 'khas' apply to speech (qawl), not actions or approvals. It also answers the potential objection that since the Sunnah is like the Quran, all reports should be mutawatir; the response is that not all reports have reached the level of tawatur, hence the need for categorization. The Hanafi school follows this tripartite division, though other schools may define them slightly differently.

Key Terms
الخبر المتواتر (al-khabar al-mutawātir): A report transmitted by a large number of narrators at every level, making collusion on falsehood impossible, yielding certain knowledge.
الخبر المشهور (al-khabar al-mashhūr): A report that was initially from one or two companions but later became widely known among the Salaf, yielding near-certainty (zann ghalib).
الخبر الآحاد (khabar al-āḥād): A report that does not reach the level of mutawatir or mashhur, transmitted by a limited number of narrators, yielding speculative knowledge (zann).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that the categories of specific and general do not apply to actions of the Prophet?
A) Because actions are not considered Sunnah
B) Because actions do not have linguistic generality or specificity
C) Because the text focuses only on speech
D) Because actions are all general

Key Takeaway
The transmission strength of a hadith determines its epistemological value: mutawatir yields certainty, mashhur yields near-certainty, ahad yields speculation.

The Tripartite Division of Khabar: Mutawatir, Mashhur, and Ahad
Introduces the division of prophetic reports based on transmission certainty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of khabar (mutawatir, mashhur, ahad) based on their epistemological certainty and state the Hanafi position that the Sunnah is equivalent to the Quran in binding authority.

Core Idea
The Sunnah is like the Quran in authority; khabar is divided by transmission certainty into mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi establishes a foundational principle of Hanafi usul: the Sunnah carries the same binding force as the Quran. However, because reports from the Prophet vary in the certainty of their transmission, they are classified into three categories. Understanding this classification is essential for evaluating the evidentiary weight of hadith in legal derivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the authority of the Sunnah
The text states that the Prophet's report (khabar) is like the Book (Quran) in obligation of knowledge and action. Cite the supporting Quranic verses (53:3-4, 59:7, 4:80).
This establishes that the Sunnah is binding like the Quran.
2
Recognize the problem of transmission uncertainty
The reason for dividing khabar is the uncertainty (shubha) in its transmission from the Prophet.
Uncertainty only exists in transmission, not in content authority.
3
List the three categories of khabar
Identify: mutawatir (no uncertainty), mashhur (slight uncertainty), ahad (probability and uncertainty).
Memorize the Arabic terms.
4
Define each type
Mutawatir: transmitted by many, impossible to falsify; Mashhur: starts as ahad, becomes widely accepted; Ahad: few narrators, contains probability of truth/falsehood.
Mashhur is a unique Hanafi category.
5
Apply the classification
Understand that mutawatir is qat'i (certain), mashhur is between qat'i and zanni (initially zanni, becomes qat'i after acceptance), ahad is zanni (probabilistic).
This affects legal rulings derived from each type.

الخبر: إنما اختار لغة الخبر ههنا دون السنة؛ لأن الأقسام من الخاص أو العام وغيرهما إنما يتأتى في القول دون الفعل. بمنزلة الكتاب: لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا يَنْطِقُ عَنِ الْهَوَى إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا وَحْيٌ يُوحَى، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا آتَاكُمُ الرَّسُولُ فَخُذُوهُ وَمَا نَهَاكُمْ عَنْهُ فَانْتَهُوا ، وقوله تعالى: ﴿مَنْ يُطِعِ الرَّسُولَ فَقَدْ أَطَاعَ اللَّهَ وغير ذلك من النصوص والأخبار مما لا تعد ولا تحصى ويجري في الحديث جميع أقسام الكتاب مما سبق، إلا أنه لم يجر فيه، وذلك للاستغناء بذكره في بحث الكتاب كذا في "الحصول". فهو كذلك: أي البحث المذكور بتمامه يأتي في قسم السنة؛ لأن قوله حجة مثل الكتاب، وهو كلام مستجمع لوجوه الفصاحة والبلاغة، فتجري فيه هذه الأقسام أيضاً. إلا أن الشبهة: جواب سوال مقدر، وهو: أن السنة فرع الكتاب في بيان تلك الأقسام بأحكامها، فلا حاجة إلى عقد باب السنة برأسها، والجواب: بأن الاشتغال بذلك لفائدة تحتاج إليها، وهي بيان اتصال السنة بالنبي ، فإنه فيه غموض لابد من انكشافه ولم يحصل إلا بما قال فيما بعد. باب الخبر إلخ جواب سوال مقدر ، وهو: أنه إذا كان خبر رسول الله بمنزلة الكتاب ينبغي أن يكون كل خبره علي متواتراً قطعياً كالكتاب، فكيف صار الخبر ثلاثة أقسام كذا قيل .. ضرب شبهة إلخ : أي نوع خفيف من نوعها فالتنوين للتحقير، وكذا إضافة الضرب إليها أي: ليس فيه شبهة
من كل وجه وقوله فيه احتمال وشبهة أي فيه احتمال قوي لصلوحه الصدق والكذب أي: فيه تجويز جانب
The report of the Messenger of God is like the Book in terms of obligation of knowledge and acting upon it. For whoever obeys him has obeyed God. So what was mentioned previously regarding the discussion of the specific and general, the common, and the ambiguous in the Book, it is likewise regarding the Sunnah, except that the uncertainty in the chapter of khabar lies in its transmission from the Messenger of God and its connection to him. For this reason, khabar is divided into three types: A type that is authentic from the Messenger of God and established without uncertainty, which is 'mutawatir'. A type in which there is a slight uncertainty, which is 'mashhur'. And a type in which there is probability and uncertainty, which is 'ahad'.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage establishes the foundational principle that the Sunnah holds the same authority as the Quran. The division of khabar into three types arises due to varying degrees of certainty in transmission. Quranic verses (53:3-4, 59:7, 4:80) are cited to prove that the Prophet's words are divinely inspired. The commentary explains that 'khabar' is used instead of 'Sunnah' because divisions apply to speech, not action. Uncertainty in transmission necessitates the tripartite division: mutawatir (absolutely certain), mashhur (widely known with some initial uncertainty), and ahad (isolated with probability of truth and falsehood).

Key Terms
الخبر (al-khabar): A report from the Prophet (PBUH) that holds authority similar to the Quran.
المتواتر (al-mutawatir): A report transmitted by a large number of narrators at each level, making collusion on falsehood impossible.
المشهور (al-mashhur): A report that starts as ahad but becomes widely accepted in the second and third generations, attaining certainty.
الآحاد (al-ahad): A report transmitted by a single or few narrators, containing probability of truth and falsehood.

C) Differences in the number of legal rulings derived from them

Key Takeaway
The Sunnah equals the Quran in authority, but reports are classified into mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad based on transmission certainty, which determines their epistemic weight in legal derivation.

Understanding Mutawatir: Definition and Conditions
Defines mutawatir and provides examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mutawatir according to Hanafi usul, identify its conditions, and explain why no specific number of narrators is required.

Core Idea
Mutawatir: certain knowledge from transmission so widespread collusion is rationally impossible.

In this lesson, we explore the definition of mutawatir, a foundational concept in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The text provides a clear definition and emphasizes that the impossibility of collusion, not a fixed number, is the key condition. You will also learn about the additional condition when applying mutawatir to the Sunnah and the examples that illustrate this type of report.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Essential Elements of Mutawatir
Extract the core components from the definition: group transmission (جماعة عن جماعة), impossibility of collusion (لا يُتصوّر توافقهم على الكذب), and large number (لكثرتهم). Note that the term 'group' is not numerically specified.
The definition in the text is concise; all elements are necessary.
2
Understand the Condition of Impossibility of Collusion
Recognize that this is a rational impossibility (استحالة عقلية). The large number makes it inconceivable that all narrators agree on a lie. This condition distinguishes mutawatir from ahad reports.
No specific number is required; the condition is contextual.
3
Note the Hanafi Position on Number
The text explicitly states that a specific number is not stipulated (لا يشترط فيه العدد) according to the verifying scholars (أهل التحقيق). This distinguishes the Hanafi view from some other schools that require a minimum (e.g., 4 or 5).
This is a key Hanafi position in usul.
4
Recognize the Additional Condition for Sunnah
The phrase 'and it reaches you in this manner' (واتصل بك هكذا) is added when defining mutawatir from the Sunnah. This ensures the chain is continuously transmitted to the listener. For mutawatir in general (like historical reports), this condition is not needed.
This restriction clarifies the scope of the definition in the text.
5
Review the Examples and the Dispute on Prophetic Mutawatir
Examples given: Quran, rak'ah numbers, zakat amounts. These are absolute mutawatir. There is a disagreement whether any specific prophetic hadith qualifies as mutawatir; some propose 'Actions are by intentions' or 'The burden of proof is on the claimant'. Understand that the dispute does not affect the definition itself.
The existence of mutawatir hadith is a secondary issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالمتواتر : ما نقله جماعة عن جماعة لا يُتصوّر توافقهم على الكذب لكثرتهم، واتصل بك هكذا.
مثاله: نقل القرآن وأعداد الركعات، ومقادير الزكاة.
السنة؛
لا يُتصوّر إلخ: أي يستحيل العقل اتفاقهم على الكذب لكثرتهم، ولا يشترط فيه العدد عند أهل التحقيق. واتصل بك: قيد به؛ لأنه في بيان المتواتر من السنة، وأما تعريف المتواتر بالنظر إلى ذاته، فلا يحتاج إلى هذا القيد كالخبر عن الملوك الخالية في الأزمنة الماضية والبلدان النائية. مثاله : أي مثال المتواتر المطلق دون المتواتر من في وجود السنة المتواترة اختلاف قيل: لم يوجد منها شيء، وقيل: هي: حديث "إنما الأعمال بالنيات"، وقيل: حديث البينة" على المدعي واليمين على من أنكر".
لأن
The mutawatir: what a group transmits from a group such that it is inconceivable that they agree upon a lie due to their large number, and it reaches you in this manner. Its example: the transmission of the Quran, the numbers of rak'ahs, and the amounts of zakat. [Commentary:] 'It is inconceivable, etc.' means that it is rationally impossible for them to agree upon a lie due to their large number, and a specific number is not stipulated according to the verifying scholars. 'And it reaches you in this manner' is a restriction because it is regarding the mutawatir from the Sunnah; as for the definition of mutawatir in itself, it does not need this restriction, like reports about ancient kings and distant lands. Its example: this is an example of absolute mutawatir, not the mutawatir from the Sunnah, regarding which there is disagreement: some say none exists, some say it is the hadith 'Actions are by intentions', and some say the hadith 'The burden of proof is on the claimant and the oath is on the one who denies'.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This lesson defines mutawatir: a report transmitted by a large group at each level, making collusion on falsehood rationally impossible. The condition 'and it reaches you in this manner' is added when speaking of mutawatir from the Sunnah to emphasize continuous transmission. The commentary clarifies that no specific number is required; what matters is the impossibility of collusion. Examples include the Quran (mutawatir in toto), the number of rak'ahs in prayer, and zakat amounts. There is a scholarly difference on whether any prophetic hadith is mutawatir; some suggest hadiths like 'Actions are by intentions' as candidates, but this is debated.

Key Terms
المتواتر (al-mutawatir): A report transmitted by such a large group at each level that collusion on falsehood is impossible.
جماعة (jama'ah): A large group of narrators that precludes collusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It must be transmitted by a group that makes collusion on a lie impossible.
C) It must be recorded in the Quran or authentic hadith collections.
D) It must be known to all Muslims.

Key Takeaway
Mutawatir transmission yields certain knowledge and does not require a specific number; it is defined by the impossibility of collusion.

The Mashhur Hadith: Definition, Conditions, and Authority
Defines mashhur and discusses its conditions, examples, and limits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mashhur, state its conditions (fame in the second/third centuries and acceptance by the Ummah), identify its epistemological status, and explain why it cannot be used to add to the Quran.

Core Idea
Mashhur starts weak but attains certainty through Ummah acceptance — yet it cannot override the Quran.

In Hanafi usul, the mashhur hadith occupies a special place between mutawatir and ahad. It begins with limited transmission but becomes so widely known and accepted by the Ummah in the early centuries that it gains binding authority. This lesson unpacks the definition, conditions, and examples from the text of Usul al-Shashi, clarifying why later fame does not qualify and why mashhur cannot add to the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its definition
Read the opening line: 'And the mashhur: what was initially like ahad, then became famous in the second and third generations, and the Ummah received it with acceptance, so it became like mutawatir until it reached you.' Paraphrase this definition in your own words.
Key elements: starting as ahad, fame in specific centuries, acceptance by the Ummah, resulting certainty.
2
List the conditions for mashhur
From the commentary, extract the conditions: (1) must become famous in the second or third century, not later; (2) must be accepted (talaqqat bi al-qabul) by the Ummah. Note that fame after the third century is disregarded.
3
Analyze the epistemological status
The text says 'so it became like mutawatir' — meaning it yields knowledge (ilm) as if it were mutawatir, but there remains some initial probability of error (shubhat al-ittisal). Understand that mashhur is a distinct category, not simply a strong ahad.
4
Apply to the examples given
Study the two examples: hadith of wiping over leather socks and hadith of stoning for adultery. Confirm that both were initially reported by a single companion but later became widely transmitted and accepted, thus qualifying as mashhur.
These are standard examples in Hanafi usul.
5
Identify the restriction: no addition to the Quran
The commentary states that mashhur cannot be used to add to the Book of God, citing the example of reciting al-Fatihah and basmalah in wudu. Understand why: the Quran's text is mutawatir beyond doubt, and a mashhur report (though strong) cannot override that certainty.
This is a key practical implication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمشهور: ما كان أوله كالآحاد ثم اشتهر في العصر الثاني والثالث وتلقته الأمة بالقبول، فصار كالمتواتر حتى اتصل بك، وذلك مثل حديث المسح على الخف والرجم في باب الزنا.
ويسمى مشهور الخلاف أي عدم ثبوته من حضرة الرسالة أقوى من تجويزه في المشهور، وفيه شبهة الاتصال منه إليك لضعف الاتصال لوحدة الراوي وفي الجماعة كمال الاتصال، وقوله: وهو الآحاد أي هو الأحاد، الواحد حديثه أيضاً كذا في "الحصول".
كالمتواتر إلخ أي في القرن الثاني والثالث واتصل بك هكذا وإنما قيدنا بالاشتهار في العصر الثاني والثالث؛ لأنه لا اعتبار للاشتهار في القرون التي بعد الثلاثة، فإن عامة أخبار الآحاد اشتهرت في هذه القرون ولا تسمى مشهورة، ولا يجوز بها الزيادة على كتاب الله تعالى مثل خبر الفاتحة والتسمية في الوضوء أو غيرهما كذا في "المعدن". حديث المسح إلخ وهو ما روي أن أحد أصحاب النبي الله قال : "كنت مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في سفر، وذكر فيه أن صلى الله عليه وسلم رسول الله مسح على خفيه". رواه البخاري ومسلم وأبو داود والترمذي والنسائي وابن ماجه، وأحمد في "مسنده" في باب المسح على الخفين. الشافي: ص ۲۱٥] والرجم في باب إلخ وهو ما روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: الثيب بالثيب جلد مائة ورجم بالحجارة" أخرجه مسلم برقم (١٦۹ ، والترمذي برقم: ١٤٣٤، وأبوداود برقم: ٤٤١٥ ، وابن ماجه برقم ٢٥٥ . [ الشافي: ص ٢١٥]
And the mashhur: what was initially like ahad, then became famous in the second and third generations, and the Ummah received it with acceptance, so it became like mutawatir until it reached you. That is like the hadith of wiping over leather socks and the hadith of stoning in the chapter of adultery. It is also called mashhur al-khilaf, meaning that the lack of its establishment from the presence of the Messenger is stronger than the probability in the mashhur, and in it there is uncertainty of connection from him to you due to weakness of connection because of the single narrator, while in the group there is complete connection. And his saying: 'and it is the ahad' means it is ahad. [Commentary:] 'Like mutawatir, etc.' means in the second and third centuries, and it reaches you in this manner. We only restricted by fame in the second and third centuries because fame in later centuries is not considered; indeed, most ahad reports became famous in these centuries and are not called mashhur, and it is not permissible to use them to add to the Book of God, like the report about al-Fatihah and the basmalah in wudu or others, as in al-Ma'din. The hadith of wiping: it is narrated that one of the companions of the Prophet said: 'I was with the Prophet on a journey, and he mentioned that the Messenger of God wiped over his leather socks.' Narrated by Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, and Ahmad in his Musnad in the chapter of wiping over leather socks. And stoning in the chapter: it is narrated that the Prophet said: 'The married adulterer receives one hundred lashes and stoning with stones.' Narrated by Muslim (no. 169), Tirmidhi (no. 1434), Abu Dawud (no. 4415), Ibn Majah (no. 255).
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This lesson defines mashhur: a report that starts with limited transmission (ahad) but becomes widely known and accepted by the Ummah in the second and third Islamic centuries, thereby attaining a status like mutawatir. Examples include the hadith of wiping over leather socks and the hadith of stoning for adultery. The commentary explains that 'mashhur' is also called 'mashhur al-khilaf' because the initial lack of certainty is stronger than the probability; there is still some uncertainty due to the single narrator at the beginning, but widespread acceptance strengthens it. Fame after the first three centuries is not considered because many ahad reports became known later but do not qualify as mashhur. Such reports cannot be used to add to the Quran, as in the dispute about reciting al-Fatihah and basmalah in prayer.

Key Terms
المشهور (al-mashhur): A report that begins as ahad but becomes widely known and accepted by the Ummah in the second and third centuries, attaining certainty.
مشهور الخلاف (mashhur al-khilaf): A term for mashhur reports where the lack of initial establishment is considered stronger than probability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the fame of a mashhur report restricted to the second and third centuries?
A) Because later narrators are less reliable
B) Because most ahad reports became famous after the third century and are not considered mashhur
C) Because the first three centuries are the only ones with authentic transmission
D) Because the Prophet forbade considering later fame

Key Takeaway
Mashhur is a distinct Hanafi category: ahad in origin, mutawatir in effect, but limited to early fame and cannot add to the Quran.

Definition and Ruling of Mutawatir Reports
Defines mutawatir and its ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of mutawatir, identify its essential elements, and explain the ruling that mutawatir yields certain knowledge.

Core Idea
Mutawatir transmission eliminates collusion, producing certainty; its denial is disbelief.

In Hanafi usul, reports vary in strength. The mutawatir is the highest category, providing unshakable certainty. This lesson unpacks its definition, conditions, and legal effect, forming the foundation for distinguishing between qat'i and zanni evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defined term
Locate the term 'al-mutawatir' in the passage and read its definition carefully.
The passage opens with 'al-mutawatir: ma naqalahu...'.
2
Deconstruct the definition components
Break down the definition: what is transmitted? By whom? Why is collusion impossible?
Focus on 'jama'atin 'an jama'atin' and 'la yutasawwaru tawafuquhum 'ala al-kadhib'.
3
Understand the added condition 'itassala bika'
The passage adds 'wa ittassala bika hakadha'. Explain why this restriction is given in the context of Sunnah.
For absolute mutawatir (e.g., historical reports), this condition is unnecessary.
4
Identify examples and the ruling
Note the examples (Qur'an, rak'ahs, Zakat) and the final ruling: mutawatir necessitates certain knowledge, its denial is kufr.
Also note the debate on whether any hadith is mutawatir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أقسام الخبر
فالمتواتر : ما نقله جماعة عن جماعة لا يُتصوّر توافقهم على الكذب لكثرتهم، واتصل بك هكذا.
مثاله: نقل القرآن وأعداد الركعات، ومقادير الزكاة.
لا يُتصوّر إلخ: أي يستحيل العقل اتفاقهم على الكذب لكثرتهم، ولا يشترط فيه العدد عند أهل التحقيق. واتصل بك: قيد به؛ لأنه في بيان المتواتر من السنة، وأما تعريف المتواتر بالنظر إلى ذاته، فلا يحتاج إلى هذا القيد كالخبر عن الملوك الخالية في الأزمنة الماضية والبلدان النائية. مثاله : أي مثال المتواتر المطلق دون المتواتر من في وجود السنة المتواترة اختلاف قيل: لم يوجد منها شيء، وقيل: هي: حديث "إنما الأعمال بالنيات"، وقيل: حديث البينة" على المدعي واليمين على من أنكر.
ثم المتواتر يوجب العلم القطعي ويكون ردّه كفراً.
Section on the divisions of reports. The mutawatir: that which a group transmits from a group, such that their collusion on a lie is inconceivable due to their large number, and it reaches you in this way. Its example: the transmission of the Qur'an, the numbers of rak'ahs, and the amounts of Zakat. 'Inconceivable etc.': i.e., the intellect deems it impossible for them to agree on a lie due to their large number, and a specific number is not stipulated according to the investigators. 'And it reaches you': restricted by this because it is in explaining the mutawatir from the Sunnah; as for the definition of mutawatir with respect to itself, it does not need this restriction, like reports about past kings in distant times and faraway lands. 'Its example': i.e., an example of absolute mutawatir, not mutawatir from [the Sunnah]; regarding the existence of mutawatir in the Sunnah, there is disagreement: some say none exist, some say the hadith 'Actions are but by intentions', and some say the hadith 'The burden of proof is on the claimant and the oath is on the denier.' Then the mutawatir necessitates certain knowledge, and its denial is disbelief.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling for mutawatir reports. The author defines mutawatir as a report transmitted by a group from a group, so numerous that collusion on a lie is inconceivable. He adds the condition that it reaches the listener in this manner, because the discussion focuses on the Sunnah. The examples given are the transmission of the Qur'an, the numbers of rak'ahs, and Zakat amounts, which are absolute mutawatir. The commentary explains that a specific number is not required; rather, the criterion is impossibility of collusion. It also notes disagreement on whether any hadith is mutawatir, mentioning candidates like 'Actions are but by intentions.' The final sentence states the ruling: mutawatir yields certain knowledge (al-'ilm al-qat'i), and rejecting it is kufr. The commentary clarifies that this certainty is absolute, unlike the lower degrees of knowledge from other report types.

Key Terms
المتواتر (al-mutawatir): A report transmitted by a group from a group such that collusion on a lie is inconceivable due to large numbers, reaching the listener in that manner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of a mutawatir report according to the passage?
A) The hadith on actions by intentions
B) The transmission of the Qur'an
C) The hadith on wiping over socks
D) The hadith on stoning

Key Takeaway
Mutawatir reports produce certain knowledge (al-'ilm al-qat'i), and rejecting them is disbelief.

Definition and Epistemological Status of Mashhur
Defines mashhur report and its epistemological ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the mashhur report and state its epistemological status (knowledge of assurance) and the ruling concerning its denier.

Core Idea
Mashhur starts solitary, gains community acceptance, yields assurance; denial is bid'a, not kufr.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, not all reports are equal. While mutawatir gives absolute certainty and ahad gives only probability, mashhur occupies a unique middle ground. It begins as a solitary report but later becomes widely transmitted and accepted by the early community, earning a status that demands action and respect. This lesson unpacks its precise definition, conditions, and the legal effect that rejecting it is an innovation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two phases
Notice that mashhur has a dual nature: initially it is a solitary (ahad) report, but later it becomes famous in the second and third generations.
The route of transmission is only strengthened over time, not weakened.
2
Verify community acceptance
The key condition is that the ummah in the eras of the Companions and Successors received it with acceptance (talaqqat bi'l-qabul). This is what elevates it above ordinary ahad.
Acceptance means acting upon it or endorsing it without objection.
3
Recognize the epistemological outcome
Mashhur produces 'ilm al-tuma'nina (knowledge of assurance) — a certitude that still has a hypothetical doubt in its origin, unlike the absolute certainty of mutawatir.
Hence its denier is not a disbeliever but commits bid'a.
4
Understand the consequence of denial
Denying mashhur implies faulting the early generations for their acceptance, which is considered an innovation (bid'a) and misguidance.
This makes mashhur binding in practice, even though its transmission history has a weak point.
5
Contrast with mutawatir
Mutawatir gives conclusive certainty (qat'i), and its denial is kufr. Mashhur's doubt is only hypothetical, so the ruling for its denier is less severe.
Both are obligatory to act upon, but their theological weight differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمشهور: ما كان أوله كالآحاد ثم اشتهر في العصر الثاني والثالث وتلقته الأمة في عصر الصحابة التابعين بالقبول، فصار كالمتواتر حتى اتصل بك، وذلك مثل حديث المسح على الخف والرجم في باب الزنا. المشهور = ويسمى خبر الخلاف أي عدم ثبوته من حضرة الرسالة أقوى من تجويزه في المشهور، وفيه شبهة الاتصال منه إليك لضعف الاتصال لوحدة الراوي وفي الجماعة كمال الاتصال، وقوله: وهو الآحاد أي هو الأحاد، الواحد حديثه أيضاً كذا في "الحصول". السنة؛ لا يُتصوّر إلخ: أي يستحيل العقل اتفاقهم على الكذب لكثرتهم، ولا يشترط فيه العدد عند أهل التحقيق. واتصل بك: قيد به؛ لأنه في بيان المتواتر من السنة، وأما تعريف المتواتر بالنظر إلى ذاته، فلا يحتاج إلى هذا القيد كالخبر عن الملوك الخالية في الأزمنة الماضية والبلدان النائية. مثاله : أي مثال المتواتر المطلق دون المتواتر من في وجود السنة المتواترة اختلاف قيل: لم يوجد منها شيء، وقيل: هي: حديث "إنما الأعمال بالنيات"، وقيل: حديث البينة" على المدعي واليمين على من أنكر. لأن كالمتواتر إلخ أي في القرن الثاني والثالث واتصل بك هكذا وإنما قيدنا بالاشتهار في العصر الثاني والثالث؛ لأنه لا اعتبار للاشتهار في القرون التي بعد الثلاثة، فإن عامة أخبار الآحاد اشتهرت في هذه القرون ولا تسمى مشهورة، ولا يجوز بها الزيادة على كتاب الله تعالى مثل خبر الفاتحة والتسمية في الوضوء أو غيرهما كذا في "المعدن". حديث المسح إلخ وهو ما روي أن أحد أصحاب النبي الله قال : "كنت مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في سفر، وذكر فيه أن صلى الله عليه وسلم رسول الله مسح على خفيه". رواه البخاري ومسلم وأبو داود والترمذي والنسائي وابن ماجه، وأحمد في "مسنده" في باب المسح على الخفين. الشافي: ص ۲۱٥] والرجم في باب إلخ وهو ما روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: الثيب بالثيب جلد مائة ورجم بالحجارة" أخرجه مسلم برقم (١٦۹ ، والترمذي برقم: ١٤٣٤، وأبوداود برقم: ٤٤١٥ ، وابن ماجه برقم ٢٥٥ . [ الشافي: ص ٢١٥] والمشهور يوجب علم الطمأنينة ويكون ردّه بدعةً، ولا خلاف بين العلماء في لزوم العمل بهما. علم الطمأنينة : أراد به العلم مع ضرب شبهة فيه صورة بالنظر إلى كونه من الآحاد في الأصل، ولذا لا يكفر جاحده كما يكفر جاحد المتواتر، وإنما العلم المستفاد به طمأنينة؛ لأنه ليسكن النفوس إليه بما ظهر له في الحال مع تمكن ضرب شبهة فيه صورة بالنظر إلى ابتدائه كذا في "المعدن". ويكون ردّه بدعةً أي إنكار المشهور بدعة؛ لأن في إنكاره تخطية لأهل العصر الثاني في قبولهم إياه، وتخطية العلماء يكون بدعة وضلالة كذا في "المعدن".
And the mashhur: that which initially was like ahad (solitary reports), then became famous in the second and third generations, and the ummah in the era of the Companions and the Successors received it with acceptance, so it became like mutawatir until it reaches you. And that is like the hadith of wiping over the socks and the hadith of stoning in the chapter of adultery. The mashhur: it is also called the report of disagreement (khabar al-khilaf), meaning that its non-establishment from the presence of the Messenger is stronger than its permissibility in the mashhur, and it contains a semblance of connection from him to you due to the weakness of connection with a single narrator, while in the group there is complete connection. And his saying: 'and it (mashhur) is ahad' means it is solitary, its narration by a single person is also (considered), as in al-Husul. The Sunnah: 'inconceivable etc.': i.e., the intellect deems it impossible for them to agree on a lie due to large numbers, and a specific number is not stipulated. 'And it reaches you': restricted because it is in explaining mutawatir from Sunnah... Its example: i.e., example of absolute mutawatir... Because 'like mutawatir etc.' means in the second and third centuries, and it reaches you in this way. We restricted with fame in the second and third centuries because fame in later centuries is not considered, for most ahad become famous in these [later] centuries but are not called mashhur, and [by such] one cannot add to the Book of Allah, like the hadith of al-Fatiha and the basmala in wudu or others, as in al-Ma'din. Hadith of wiping etc.: ... 'Stoning in the chapter etc.': ... And the mashhur necessitates the knowledge of assurance (tuma'nina), and its denial is bid'a, and there is no disagreement among scholars regarding the obligation of acting upon both (mutawatir and mashhur). 'Knowledge of assurance': he means knowledge with a semblance of doubt in form, considering its origin as ahad, and therefore its denier is not declared a disbeliever like the denier of mutawatir. The knowledge derived from it is assurance because the soul finds tranquility in it based on what appears in the immediate context, while a semblance of doubt remains in form considering its beginning, as in al-Ma'din. 'And its denial is bid'a': i.e., rejecting mashhur is innovation because in its rejection lies faulting the people of the second generation for their acceptance, and faulting scholars is innovation and misguidance, as in al-Ma'din.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage defines mashhur and sets its ruling. Mashhur begins as a solitary (ahad) report but becomes widely known in the second and third generations, and the ummah accepts it, making it like mutawatir in its connection. Examples are the hadiths on wiping over socks and stoning for adultery. The commentary explains that mashhur is also called 'khabar al-khilaf' because its non-attribution to the Prophet is more likely than its attribution, but it still carries a semblance of connection. The ruling is that mashhur yields knowledge of assurance (al-'ilm al-tuma'nina)—a certainty with a hypothetical doubt regarding its origin—so its denier commits bid'a, not kufr. The text emphasizes that all scholars agree on the obligation to act upon both mutawatir and mashhur. The commentary further clarifies that the rejecter of mashhur faults the early community's acceptance, which is bid'a.

Key Terms
المشهور (al-mashhur): A report initially ahad that becomes widely transmitted in the second and third generations and accepted by the ummah, becoming like mutawatir in connection.
علم الطمأنينة (al-'ilm al-tuma'nina): Knowledge of assurance; a certitude that still carries a hypothetical doubt about its origin, as opposed to the absolute certainty of mutawatir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence of denying a mashhur report?
A) It is kufr (disbelief)
B) It is fasiq (sin)
C) It is bid'a (innovation)
D) It is permissible

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, mashhur is a distinct category: it provides knowledge of assurance, and rejecting it is a blameworthy innovation, though not disbelief.

Definition and Ruling of Khabar al-Wahid
Defines ahad, its ruling, and conditions for acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khabar al-wahid, explain its ruling in Hanafi usul, and list the conditions for its acceptance.

Core Idea
Khabar al-wahid necessitates action, not certainty — a core Hanafi distinction.

In Hanafi usul, not all reports have the same authority. Some are mass-transmitted (mutawatir) and yield certain knowledge; others are solitary (khabar al-wahid) and only obligate action. This lesson unpacks the definition of khabar al-wahid, its legal effect, and the strict conditions a narrator must meet for the report to be binding. Understanding this distinction is key to knowing when a hadith can be used as proof and what degree of conviction it provides.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Definition
Read the definition carefully: 'ما نقله واحد عن واحد، أو واحد عن جماعة، أو جماعة عن واحد ولا عبرة للعدد إذا لم تبلغ حد المشهور.' Note that multiplicity of transmitters does not elevate it to mashhur.
The definition emphasizes that even many transmitters can still produce a khabar wahid if they fall short of the mashhur threshold.
2
Distinguish the Ruling
The text states: 'وهو يوجب العمل به في الأحكام الشرعية' — it necessitates action. It does not produce knowledge. The denier is not a disbeliever.
This is the Hanafi position; Ahmad holds it yields certain knowledge.
3
List the Conditions
The conditions for acceptance: Islam of the narrator, uprightness (adala), precision (dabt), sanity, and connection (ittisal) to the Prophet.
These conditions ensure reliability; missing any prevents obligation.
4
Explore Precision (Dabt)
Dabt is defined as proper hearing, correct understanding, diligent memorization, and continuous review until transmission.
A narrator whose forgetfulness is predominant is not accepted.
5
Analyze the Dispute
The text reports that Ahmad and most hadith scholars say khabar wahid yields certain knowledge (ilm al-yaqin). The Hanafi response is based on phenomenological observation: we do not find certainty in ourselves from ahad reports.
The practical implication: for Hanafis, khabar wahid obliges action but does not produce conviction; rejecting it is not disbelief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما الكلام في الآحاد فنقول: خبر الواحد هو ما نقله واحد عن واحد، أو واحد عن جماعة، أو جماعة عن واحد ولا عبرة للعدد إذا لم تبلغ حد المشهور.
وهو يوجب العمل به في الأحكام الشرعية بشرط إسلام الراوي وعدالته، وضبطه، وعقله، واتصاله بك ذلك من رسول الله عليلها بهذا الشرط.
سمي علم الطمأنينة : أراد به العلم مع ضرب شبهة فيه صورة بالنظر إلى كونه من الآحاد في الأصل، ولذا لا يكفر جاحده كما يكفر جاحد المتواتر، وإنما العلم المستفاد به طمأنينة؛ لأنه ليسكن النفوس إليه بما ظهر له في الحال مع تمكن ضرب شبهة فيه صورة بالنظر إلى ابتدائه كذا في "المعدن". ويكون ردّه بدعةً أي إنكار المشهور بدعة؛ لأن في إنكاره تخطية لأهل العصر الثاني في قبولهم إياه، وتخطية العلماء يكون بدعة وضلالة كذا في "المعدن". ولا عبرة للعدد أي لا اعتبار لكثرة العدد إذا كان دون كثرة عدد المشهور يعني لا يخرج بهذه الكثرة عن كونه خبراً واحداً. وهو يوجب العمل إلخ: أي حكم خبر الواحد أنه يوجب العمل، ولا يوجب العلم لا علم اليقين ولا علم الطمأنينة، وهذا مذهب أكثر أهل العلم وجملة الفقهاء وذهب أحمد وأكثر المحدثين إلى أنه يوجب علم اليقين، وهذا خلاف ما نجد في أنفسنا من أخبار الآحاد ووجوب العمل إنما يثبت بشرط إسلام الراوي وعدالته، وضبطه وعقله وغيرها، فلا يجب العمل بخبر الكافر والفاسق، وكذا لا يجب العمل بخبر الصبي والمعتوه؛ لفقدان الشروط، ولا يجب العمل بخبر الذي اشتدت غفلته بأن كان سهوه ونسيانه أغلب من حفظه. إسلام الراوي: وهو شرط للأداء لا للتحمل. [ حاشية الشيخ أكرم الندوي ص ١٩٥] وضبطه: أي سماع الكلام حق سماعه والفهم بمعناه الذي أريد به، ثم حفظه ببذل الجهد، ثم الثبات عليه بمحافظة حدوده ومراقبته بمذاكرته على إساءة الظن بنفسه إلى حين أدائه كذا في "المعدن". بهذا الشرط المذكور من كونه مسلماً عادلاً.
The discussion is only regarding ahad (solitary reports). We say: Khabar al-wahid is that which is transmitted by one from one, or one from a group, or a group from one, and multiplicity is not considered if it does not reach the level of mashhur. It necessitates action upon it in legal rulings, with the condition of the narrator being Muslim, upright (adil), precise (dabit), sane, and its connection to you from the Messenger of Allah through this condition. 'Knowledge of assurance': he means knowledge with a semblance of doubt in form, considering its origin as ahad, and therefore its denier is not declared a disbeliever as the denier of mutawatir is. The knowledge derived from it is assurance because the soul finds tranquility in it based on what appears in the immediate context, while a semblance of doubt remains in form considering its beginning, as in al-Ma'din. 'And its denial is bid'a': i.e., rejecting mashhur is innovation... 'And multiplicity is not considered': i.e., the large number is not considered if it is below the number of mashhur, meaning it does not exit its status as khabar wahid. 'And it necessitates action etc.': i.e., the ruling of khabar wahid is that it necessitates action, not knowledge—neither certainty nor assurance. This is the madhhab of most scholars and the majority of jurists. Ahmad and most hadith scholars hold that it necessitates certain knowledge. This contradicts what we find in ourselves regarding ahad reports. The obligation of action is established only with the conditions of the narrator being Muslim, upright, precise, sane, etc. So the report of a disbeliever or a sinner is not obligated to be acted upon, nor the report of a child or insane person due to lack of conditions, nor the report of one who is extremely heedless such that his forgetfulness outweighs his memory. 'Islam of the narrator': it is a condition for performance, not for bearing. [Footnote: from Shaykh Akram al-Nadwi, p. 195] 'And his precision': i.e., hearing the speech properly, understanding its intended meaning, then memorizing it with effort, then adhering to it by preserving its limits and reviewing it despite thinking ill of oneself until its performance, as in al-Ma'din. With these conditions mentioned of being Muslim and upright.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage defines khabar al-wahid and discusses its ruling and conditions. Khabar al-wahid is transmitted by one narrator from one, or one from many, or many from one, and it does not reach the level of mashhur. Its ruling: it necessitates action (wujub al-'amal) in legal matters, but does not yield knowledge—neither certainty nor assurance. It requires conditions in the narrator: Islam, uprightness ('adala), precision (dabt), sanity, and connection to the Prophet. The commentary explains that the denier of a khabar wahid is not declared a disbeliever, and that the majority of scholars (including the Hanafis) hold that it does not produce certainty. It notes a dispute: Ahmad ibn Hanbal and most hadith scholars hold it produces certain knowledge. The conditions are elaborated: the narrator must be a discerning adult Muslim, upright, precise in hearing, understanding, memorizing, and preserving the hadith. The report of a child, insane, or forgetful person is not accepted. Precision is further defined as proper hearing, understanding, retention, and careful review.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by one from one, one from many, or many from one, not reaching mashhur level.
الضبط (al-dabt): Precision: hearing correctly, understanding the intended meaning, memorizing with effort, and preserving through review.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for accepting a khabar wahid according to the passage?
A) The narrator must be Muslim
B) The narrator must be upright (adil)
C) The report must be transmitted by at least two narrators
D) The narrator must be precise (dabit)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, khabar al-wahid obligates action but does not yield certainty; its acceptance depends on the narrator's Islam, integrity, precision, sanity, and continuity.

Types of Khabar and Conditions of Khabar al-Wahid
Definition of khabar types and conditions for khabar al-wahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad, state the Hanafi position that khabar al-wahid obliges action not knowledge, and identify the conditions for accepting khabar al-wahid.

Core Idea
Khabar al-wahid obliges action but not certain knowledge; rejecting it is not disbelief.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi lays the foundation for understanding how the Hanafi school treats different types of reports. We will distinguish between mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad, and learn the precise conditions a narrator must meet for a solitary report to be binding in practice.

Guided Path
1
Classify the three types of khabar
Identify mutawatir (mass-transmitted, certain knowledge), mashhur (well-known, knowledge of tranquility), and ahad (solitary, action only). Note the consequences of rejection for each.
Mutawatir rejection = kufr; mashhur rejection = bid'a; ahad rejection = not kufr.
2
Define khabar al-wahid
Understand the definition: a report transmitted by one from one, one from a group, or a group from one, not reaching the level of mashhur.
The number of narrators is irrelevant if below mashhur.
3
State the Hanafi ruling on khabar al-wahid
Khabar al-wahid obliges action (wujub al-'amal) but does not give knowledge—neither certain nor tranquility.
This is the position of 'most scholars and generality of jurists'.
4
List the conditions for acceptance
The narrator must be Muslim, just (`adil), precise (dabt), sane (`aqil), and the chain must be connected to the Prophet (ﷺ). Lack of any condition negates obligation.
Islam is a condition for performance (ada') not for bearing (tahammul).
5
Note the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam Ahmad and most muhaddithun hold that khabar al-wahid gives certain knowledge. The Hanafis argue from internal experience ('we do not find certainty').
The practical difference: denier of khabar al-wahid is not a disbeliever in Hanafi view.

Source Text

فصل في أقسام الخبر
ثم المتواتر يوجب العلم القطعي ويكون ردّه كفراً.
والمشهور يوجب علم الطمأنينة ويكون ردّه بدعةً، ولا خلاف بين العلماء في لزوم العمل بهما.
وإنما الكلام في الآحاد فنقول: خبر الواحد هو ما نقله واحد عن واحد، أو واحد عن جماعة، أو جماعة عن واحد ولا عبرة للعدد إذا لم تبلغ حد المشهور.
وهو يوجب العمل به في الأحكام الشرعية بشرط إسلام الراوي وعدالته، وضبطه، وعقله، واتصاله بك ذلك من رسول الله عليه‌السلام بهذا الشرط.
سمي
علم الطمأنينة : أراد به العلم مع ضرب شبهة فيه صورة بالنظر إلى كونه من الآحاد في الأصل، ولذا لا يكفر جاحده كما يكفر جاحد المتواتر، وإنما العلم المستفاد به طمأنينة؛ لأنه ليسكن النفوس إليه بما ظهر له في الحال مع تمكن ضرب شبهة فيه صورة بالنظر إلى ابتدائه كذا في "المعدن". ويكون ردّه بدعةً أي إنكار المشهور بدعة؛ لأن في إنكاره تخطية لأهل العصر الثاني في قبولهم إياه، وتخطية العلماء يكون بدعة وضلالة كذا في "المعدن". ولا عبرة للعدد أي لا اعتبار لكثرة العدد إذا كان دون كثرة عدد المشهور يعني لا يخرج بهذه الكثرة عن كونه خبراً واحداً. وهو يوجب العمل إلخ: أي حكم خبر الواحد أنه يوجب العمل، ولا يوجب العلم لا علم اليقين ولا علم الطمأنينة، وهذا مذهب أكثر أهل العلم وجملة الفقهاء وذهب أحمد وأكثر المحدثين إلى أنه يوجب علم اليقين، وهذا خلاف ما نجد في أنفسنا من أخبار الآحاد ووجوب العمل إنما يثبت بشرط إسلام الراوي وعدالته، وضبطه وعقله وغيرها، فلا يجب العمل بخبر الكافر والفاسق، وكذا لا يجب العمل بخبر الصبي والمعتوه؛ لفقدان الشروط، ولا يجب العمل بخبر الذي اشتدت غفلته بأن كان سهوه ونسيانه أغلب من حفظه. إسلام الراوي: وهو شرط للأداء لا للتحمل. [ حاشية الشيخ أكرم الندوي ص ١٩٥] وضبطه: أي سماع الكلام حق سماعه والفهم بمعناه الذي أريد به، ثم حفظه ببذل الجهد، ثم الثبات عليه بمحافظة حدوده ومراقبته بمذاكرته على إساءة الظن بنفسه إلى حين أدائه كذا في "المعدن". بهذا الشرط المذكور من كونه مسلماً عادلاً.
Section on the divisions of khabar. Then the mutawatir obliges certain knowledge, and rejecting it is disbelief. The mashhur obliges knowledge of tranquility, and rejecting it is innovation, and there is no disagreement among scholars regarding the necessity of acting upon both. The discussion is only about ahad. We say: Khabar al-wahid is what a single person narrates from a single person, or a single person from a group, or a group from a single person; and there is no consideration of number unless it reaches the level of mashhur. It obliges action in shari rulings on the condition that the narrator be Muslim, just, precise, intelligent, and that it be connected to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) with these conditions. 'Ilm al-tuma'nina is intended as knowledge with a shade of doubt in form with respect to its being from ahad in origin, hence its denier is not declared a disbeliever as the denier of mutawatir is. Rejecting it is innovation: denial of mashhur is innovation because in its denial lies faulting the people of the second generation for accepting it, and faulting scholars is innovation and misguidance. 'No consideration for number' means no weight for multiplicity if it is below the multiplicity of mashhur; i.e., it does not exit ahad status by this multiplicity. 'It obliges action etc.': the ruling of khabar al-wahid is that it obliges action, not knowledge—neither certain knowledge nor knowledge of tranquility. This is the madhhab of most scholars and the generality of jurists. Ahmad and most muhaddithun hold that it obliges certain knowledge, but this contradicts what we find in ourselves from ahad reports. Obligation of action is established only on condition of the narrator being Muslim, just, precise, intelligent, etc. Hence the report of an unbeliever or a fasiq is not acted upon, nor the report of a child or an insane person due to the lack of conditions, nor the report of one whose heedlessness is severe such that his forgetfulness predominates over his memory. The Islam of the narrator is a condition for performance, not for bearing. Footnotes: dabt means hearing the words properly, understanding their intended meaning, then memorizing them with effort, then preserving them by guarding their limits and reviewing them while suspecting oneself until the time of narration. With these mentioned conditions of being Muslim and just.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a definition and categorization of types of khabar (reports) in Hanafi usul. The author first distinguishes between mutawatir (mass-transmitted) which gives certain knowledge and rejecting it is kufr, and mashhur (well-known) which gives knowledge of tranquility (ilm al-tuma'nina) and rejecting it is bid'a. Both are agreed upon for action. Then the focus shifts to khabar al-wahid (solitary report), which is defined as a report narrated by a single person from a single person, or a single from a group, or a group from a single, as long as it does not reach the level of mashhur. The key point is that khabar al-wahid obliges action in shari rulings but does not produce certain knowledge, contrary to the view of Ahmad ibn Hanbal and many muhaddithun who hold it gives certain knowledge. The Hanafi position is based on the fact that we do not find certainty in ourselves from ahad reports. The conditions for acceptance are: the narrator must be Muslim, 'adil (just), dabt (precise and reliable memory), 'aql (sane), and the chain must be connected to the Prophet (ﷺ). Additional conditions exclude reports from disbelievers, fasiqs, children, the insane, and extremely forgetful narrators. The text also notes that narrator's Islam is a condition for performance (ada') not for bearing (tahammul). The commentary elaborates on dabt as correct hearing, understanding, memorization, and preservation.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): ما نقله واحد عن واحد، أو واحد عن جماعة، أو جماعة عن واحد دون حد المشهور
علم الطمأنينة (ilm al-tuma'nina): العلم مع ضرب شبهة في الصورة، أي ظن قوي مع احتمال خفي
ضبط (dabt): سماع الكلام، وفهم معناه، وحفظه بجهد، والثبات عليه بالمذاكرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi usul, what is the legal status of khabar al-wahid?
A) It obliges both knowledge and action.
B) It obliges action but not knowledge.
C) It obliges knowledge but not action.
D) It is rejected.

Key Takeaway
Khabar al-wahid is a binding source for action only, not for certain knowledge, under strict conditions of narrator reliability.
