Accepting Single Report in Fosterage and Similar Cases
Applies the principle of accepting single report when it does not contradict the apparent, with fosterage example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a single report (khabar al-wahid) is accepted in Hanafi usul and distinguish between cases where it does not contradict the apparent, using the example of fosterage.

Core Idea
A single report is accepted when it does not contradict an apparent reality; fosterage after marriage is such a case, while fosterage before marriage is not.

In this passage, the author extends the principle that a single report (khabar al-wahid) is a proof (hujja) in certain contexts, provided it does not contradict an apparent state of affairs. The key example is fosterage (rada') that occurs after marriage: a trustworthy person's report that the wife was breastfed by the husband's mother or sister is accepted because it does not contradict the public knowledge of the marriage. This contrasts with fosterage claimed before marriage, which would contradict the apparent and is therefore not accepted. The passage also discusses similar cases (death/divorce report, qibla direction, water purity) and engages with the Shafi'i disagreement on whether a single woman's testimony suffices in fosterage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
The core principle is that a single report (khabar al-wahid) is accepted if it does not contradict an apparent reality (al-zahir). Recognize that this is an expansion of the general acceptance of khabar al-wahid in Hanafi usul.
2
Analyze the Fosterage Example
Examine the case of fosterage after marriage (al-rada' al-tari'i). The marriage is public (zahir), but the fosterage could have occurred privately later—no contradiction. Contrast with fosterage before marriage, which would contradict the public marriage and thus is rejected.
The principle is applied to distinguish between acceptable and unacceptable reports.
3
Extend to Other Cases
The author extends the same logic to a woman hearing of her husband's death/divorce, qibla direction, and water impurity. In each, there is no apparent evidence contradicting the report, so the single report is accepted and acted upon.
These are legal applications where reliance on a single report is permitted.
4
Explore the Madhhab Dispute
The passage reports a dispute: the Hanafi position (and Ahmad, Ishaq) accepts a single woman's report in fosterage based on the hadith of 'Uqbah ibn al-Harith. The Shafi'i school requires two witnesses for testimony. Understand the distinction between khabar (report for fatwa) and shahada (testimony in court).
The Hanafi response emphasizes that fosterage is a matter of khabar, not shahada, so the usual witness count does not apply.
5
Conclude on the Role of Zahir
The decisive factor is whether the report contradicts the apparent (zahir). Where there is no contradiction, the single report is accepted for fatwa and practice; but for testimony (shahada), stricter rules apply.
This illustrates how Hanafi usul balances textual evidence with practical presumptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالرضاع الطارئ: أي على النكاح بأن تزوج رجل صغيرة فأخبر ثقة أنها قد ارتضعت من أمه أو أخته يجوز الاعتماد على خبره، فتحرم الصغيرة على الزوج؛ لأنها صارت أخته رضاعاً.
وكذلك إذا أُخبرت المرأة بموت زوجها أو طلاقه إياها وهو غائب جاز أن تعتمد على مثل أخبار الرضاع خبره وتتزوج بغيره.
ولو اشتبهت عليه القبلة فأخبره واحد عنها وجب العمل به، ولو وجد ماء لا يعلَمُ حاله الإنسان أي القبلة فأخبره واحدٌ عن النجاسة لا يتوضأ به بل يتيمم.
فصل في حجية خبر الواحد
خبر الواحد حجةٌ في أربعة مواضع:
النبي
لا يقبل خبره: فلا يحكم ببطلان العقد وتفريقهما بمجرد خبرها أنها أرضعتها، فلا يتزوج بأختها؛ لأن خبرها مخالف للظاهر؛ لأن النكاح حصل بشهرة وحضور جماعة، فلو كان الرضاع ثابتاً لم يخف عليهما وعلى الشهود وأقربائهما أن بينهما سبب حرمته، ومن حيث أنه لم يشتهر دل أنه غير صحيح، بخلاف الرضاع الطارئ؛ لأنه لا يخالف الظاهر، ثم هذا كله فتوى وقضاء، وأما التقوى والديانة فهو أن يدعها لهذه الشبهة، وقد أخرج الترمذي في "سننه" عن عقبة بن الحارث أنه تزوج امرأة فجاءت امرأة سوداء قالت إني أرضعتكما، قال: فأتيت فقلت: تزوجت فلانة بنت فلان فجاءتنا امرأة سوداء، فقالت: إني أرضعتكما وهي كاذبة، قال: فأعرض عني قال فأتيته من قبل وجهه فقلت إنها كاذبة قال: وكيف بها وقد زعمت أنها قد أرضعتكما دعها عنك، قال: وهذا حديث حسن صحيح، والعمل على هذا عند بعض أهل العلم من أصحاب النبي ومن بعدهم أجازوا شهادة المرأة الواحدة في الرضاع وبه يقول أحمد وإسحاق وقال بعض أهل العلم: لا يجوز شهادة امرأة واحدة في الرضاع، وهو قول الشافعي له، فالجمهور على أنه لا يثبت إلا بنصاب الشهادة فافهم كذا في "الحصول". جاز أن تعتمد إلخ لعدم مخالفة الظاهر؛ لأنه ليس همه دليل مكذب الخبر الواحد، فيقبل خبره ووجب العمل به، ثم اعلم أن هذا في الأخبار، وأما في الشهادة فلا يصح وإن كان الشاهد اثنين، حيث لا يقضي القاضي بالفرقة؛ لأنه قضاء على الغائب كذا في "النهاية". خبر الواحد: أي الواحد الشرعي الذي لم يبلغ حد الشهرة والتواتر لا الواحد الحقيقي، فتدخل فيه شهادة الشاهدين أو أربعة من الشهداء كما في الزنا.
في أربعة مواضع ولم يذكر الماتن حلقه القسم الخامس الذي ذكره سائر الأصوليين وهو ما كان عقوبة من حقوق الله تعالى؛ لأن خبر الواحد ليس بحجة فيه؛ لأن إثبات العقوبات كالحدود والقصاص لا يجوز بالشبهات فإذا تمكن في الدليل شبهة لم يجز إثباتها به.
With the fosterage that occurs after marriage: i.e., after the marriage, when a man marries a young girl, and a trustworthy person informs that she had been breastfed by his mother or sister, it is permissible to rely on his report, so the young girl becomes forbidden to the husband because she has become his sister through fosterage. Similarly, if a woman is informed of her husband's death or his divorce of her while he is absent, she may rely on such news and marry another. If a person is uncertain about the qibla and a single person informs him of it, it is obligatory to act upon it. If he finds water whose condition he does not know, and a single person informs him of its impurity, he does not perform wudu with it but rather does tayammum. Section on the authority of the single report: The single report is a proof in four places: ... his report is not accepted: so the invalidity of the contract is not judged upon [and] separation between them is not made merely by her report that she had breastfed them, so he does not marry her sister, because her report contradicts the apparent; for the marriage occurred with publicity and the presence of a group. So if the fosterage were established, it would not have been hidden from them and from the witnesses and their relatives that there is a cause of unlawfulness between them. Since it did not become widespread, it indicates that it is unsound. Unlike fosterage that occurs after marriage, because it does not contradict the apparent. Then all this is for fatwa and judgment. As for piety and religiousness, he should leave her due to this doubt. At-Tirmidhi narrated in his Sunan from 'Uqbah ibn al-Harith that he married a woman, then a black woman came and said: I breastfed both of you. He said: I came and said: I married so-and-so daughter of so-and-so, then a black woman came and said 'I breastfed both of you,' and she is lying. He said: So he turned away from me. I came from in front of his face and said: She is lying. He said: How can that be when she claimed she breastfed both of you? Leave her. He said: This hadith is hasan sahih. Action upon this is according to some scholars among the Companions and those after them; they permitted the testimony of a single woman in fosterage, and Ahmad and Ishaq also hold this. Some scholars said: The testimony of a single woman in fosterage is not permissible, and that is the saying of Ash-Shafi'i. The majority hold that it is not established except with the required number of witnesses. Understand it, as in al-Husul. It is permissible for her to rely etc. due to lack of contradiction to the apparent, because there is no evidence that refutes the single report, so his report is accepted and action upon it is obligatory. Then know that this is in reports (akhbar), but as for testimony (shahada), it is not valid even if there are two witnesses, because the judge does not rule for separation, as it is a ruling against the absent, as in an-Nihaya. The single report: meaning the legally single report that has not reached the level of shuhra and tawatur, not the literally single person. So it includes the testimony of two witnesses or four witnesses as in zina. In four places: the author did not mention the fifth category mentioned by other usuliyyun, which is that which is a punishment from the rights of Allah; because the single report is not a proof for it, for establishing punishments such as hudud and qisas is not permissible with doubts. So if a doubt is present in the evidence, it is not permissible to establish them with it.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage provides detailed applications of the previously stated principle. It begins by explaining the fosterage (rada) example in more depth. If a trustworthy person reports that a man's wife was breastfed by the man's mother or sister after the marriage (al-rada' al-tari'i), that report is accepted because it does not contradict the apparent. The marriage took place with publicity, but the fosterage could have occurred later, so there is no inherent contradiction. However, if the report claims the fosterage occurred before marriage, then it contradicts the apparent (the public wedding), so the report is not accepted. The author then cites a hadith from 'Uqbah ibn al-Harith to show that the Prophet accepted a single woman's report about fosterage, at least from a pious perspective, although the majority of scholars (including Shafi'i) require two witnesses for testimony. The passage also mentions other cases where a single report is accepted: a woman hearing of her husband's death or divorce, a person being informed of the qibla direction, and a person being told that water is impure. In all these, the report does not contradict any apparent evidence. Then it transitions into the section on the authority of khabar al-wahid, stating it is a proof in four places (but the author of the matn, presumably the matn of Usul al-Shashi, did not list a fifth category which is punishments, because in such cases doubt prevents enforcement). The commentary clarifies that 'single report' here means a report that has not reached the level of widespread transmission or tawatur, and includes reports from two or more witnesses as long as they are below the threshold of tawatur.

Key Terms
الرضاع الطارئ (al-rada' al-tari'i): Fosterage that occurs after the marriage, not before.
خبر الواحد الشرعي (khabar al-wahid al-shar'i): A report that has not reached the level of tawatur or shuhra, even if transmitted by multiple people (e.g., two or four witnesses).
شهادة (shahada): Testimony in court with specific conditions, as opposed to khabar (report) which is for fatwa.
الظاهر (al-zahir): The apparent state of affairs that is publicly known or evident.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a single report about fosterage after marriage accepted but a report about fosterage before marriage not accepted?
A) Because the report about fosterage after marriage is more reliable
B) Because fosterage after marriage does not contradict the apparent, while fosterage before marriage contradicts the public knowledge of the marriage
C) Because the Sahaba widely reported fosterage after marriage
D) Because the hadith only mentions fosterage after marriage

Key Takeaway
A single report (khabar al-wahid) is accepted in Hanafi usul when it does not contradict an apparent reality (zahir); this principle governs the acceptance of reports in fosterage, divorce, qibla, and similar cases, and distinguishes between fatwa and testimony.

Classification of Reports by Legal Subject (Hanafi Usul)
Classification of khabar into four types by legal subject

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify reports (khabar) into the four Hanafi categories based on legal subject and state the required conditions (number/justice) for each type.

Core Idea
Reports are accepted based on legal matter: worship and disputes need multiple just narrators; transactions accept even a single immoral narrator; intermediate matters require either number or justice.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi presents a foundational classification in Hanafi usul: the type of legal matter determines when a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) is accepted. The madhhab distinguishes four categories—acts of worship, disputes, transactions, and intermediate matters—each with its own conditions of number and justice. Understanding these categories is essential for evaluating the binding force of reported evidence in different contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
From the text, locate the four types: (1) pure acts of worship (ibadat) implied by the mention of the second, (2) disputes (munaza'at), (3) transactions (mu'amalat), (4) dismissal/interdiction (azl/hajr).
The first type is not explicitly numbered but is referenced as 'the second' and the following.
2
Extract the conditions for each category
For type 2 (disputes): both adad (number, i.e., two) and adalat (justice) are required. For type 3 (transactions): a single report is accepted from anyone, just or immoral. For type 4 (azl/hajr): either number or justice suffices. Type 1 (ibadat) implicitly requires both, as indicated by the condition for testimony on the crescent moon.
The text explicitly states conditions for the second, third, and fourth; the first is derived from the commentary.
3
Understand the rationale
Disputes require heightened conditions due to prevalence of forgery (tazwir). Transactions relax conditions due to necessity (darura) – people rarely find fully qualified witnesses. Azl and hajr are midway, so either condition suffices.
The text mentions 'al-tazdir wa al-talabis' (forgery and deception) for disputes and 'al-darura' for transactions.
4
Apply the classification
Given a scenario, determine the legal matter and then decide whether a report is sufficient. For instance, a report about a gift (transaction) is accepted from a single person, even a fasiq; a report about a sale (dispute) requires two just witnesses.
Use the examples from the text: sales (buyu'), beverages (ashriba), absolute properties (amlak al-mursala) for disputes; gifts (hadiyya) for transactions.

The Second Research on the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah. As for the second: number and justice are required in it. Its example: 'disputes'. As for the third: the report of a single person, whether just or immoral, is accepted in it. Its example: 'transactions'. As for the fourth: either number or justice is required in it according to Abu Hanifa and his followers, and its example: 'dismissal and interdiction'. Section on the authority of the single-narrator report. [Commentary] His report is not binding for fasting; rather the binding is the text, and it is answered that the author's place in it follows Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, and that is correct, for justice is a condition in testimony regarding the crescent of Ramadan, and the report of an immoral person is accepted in the third type as will come, thus in al-Ma'din. As for the second, which is purely the right of the servant, there is no pure obligation in it. Disputes like sales, beverages, and absolute properties: that one claims against another that he sold this slave or bought that, or that a thousand is owed to him, then number and justice are required in it. The first by His saying: 'And call to witness two witnesses' [Quran], and the second by His saying: 'And call to witness two just persons among you'. And because forgery, deception, and tricks are more in disputes, so the condition of increased number and the word 'testimony' was imposed to minimize them and safeguard inviolable rights as far as possible. And because a dispute is between two with two contradictory reports from claim and idea, so separation and preference are not achieved by the genus of the report but by a report that shows an advantage over another, by oath or testimony: i.e., statements of two or more, thus in al-Ma'din. So the report is accepted in it, etc.: for indeed in gifts, the gift is accepted from the just and the immoral by their informing that it is a gift, because necessity calls for accepting the report of every discerning person, for a person rarely finds those who combine all conditions of testimony, and there is no evidence for the listener except this report, so the conditions fall away except discernment due to necessity, contrary to his report against it, for there is no necessity to accept the report of the immoral person because of the abundance of just narrators and the ruling of Allah in that incident can be known by another evidence, i.e., analogy, thus in al-Ma'din. And its example: dismissal and interdiction, i.e., dismissal of an agent and interdiction of a permitted minor, for in them there is obligation in that it binds them to a thousand and invalidates their knowledge in the future, and it is not an obligation in that the principal and the guardian act in his right by revocation just as they act in his right by agency and permission, so we required number and justice in them because they are between the two statuses, thus in al-Ma'din. About
acting
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage from the matn (core text) of Usul al-Shashi categorises reports (khabar) into four types based on the nature of the legal matter. The first type is implied from the mention of the second; it concerns pure acts of worship (ibadat) where number and justice are required. The second type (explicitly mentioned) applies to disputes (munaza'at) such as sales, drinks, and absolute claims of ownership; here both number of witnesses (two) and their justice are required, supported by Quranic verses. The third type applies to transactions (mu'amalat) like gifts; here a single person's report is accepted whether he is just or immoral, due to necessity—people rarely find fully qualified witnesses, and the information is vital. The fourth type includes matters like dismissal of an agent (azl) and interdiction of a permitted minor (hajr al-ma'dhun); these are midway between pure rights of Allah and pure rights of men, so either number or justice suffices according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The commentary from al-Ma'din elaborates on each type, citing Quranic proofs and rational justifications (e.g., prevalence of forgery in disputes). It also clarifies that in matters like fasting (first type), justice is required for testimony about the crescent moon, but the report of an immoral person is not accepted. This classification is fundamental in Hanafi usul for understanding when a khabar al-wahid is binding.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by a single person, whose acceptance conditions vary by legal subject.
عدد (adad): The required number of reporters or witnesses, e.g., two in disputes.
عدالة (adalat): Justice or trustworthiness of the reporter; a condition in some types.
المنازعات (al-munaza'at): Disputes and litigation, where both number and justice are required.
المعاملات (al-mu'amalat): Transactions such as gifts, where a single report suffices even from an immoral person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which type of legal matter is the report of a single person, whether just or immoral, accepted?
A) Disputes (المنازعات)
B) Transactions (المعاملات)
C) Pure acts of worship
D) Dismissal and interdiction

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of a report in Hanafi usul depends on the legal subject: acts of worship and disputes require two just witnesses; transactions accept any discerning person; dismissal/interdiction requires either number or justice.

Qiyas on the Cat's Su'r: Extending Purity via 'Illa of Tawwaf
Qiyas and ikhtilaf on cat's su'r

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the 'illa in the hadith of Ali and apply qiyas jali to derive the ruling for similar household animals.

Core Idea
The cat's frequent movement (tawwaf) justifies extending purity to its leftover water and to other household pests via qiyas.

The cat is a common household animal, and its saliva (su'r) has been a subject of legal discussion. In this passage, we see how the Hanafi school uses a hadith from Imam Ali (RA) to establish the purity of the cat's leftover water and then extends this ruling to other animals like mice and snakes through analogical reasoning (qiyas). This lesson will walk you through the derivation chain, from the textual proof to the final ruling, and highlight the differences among scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source text and its authority
Locate the hadith of Ali (RA) and note its chain and strength. The hadith explicitly states the cat is not impure and gives the reason: 'it is one of those that go around you.'
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
2
Extract the 'illa from the text
The word 'tawwafin' indicates frequent movement and presence in the house. This is identified as the effective cause ('illa) for the ruling of purity.
Tahqiq al-manat: determining the 'illa from the explicit text.
3
Apply qiyas to other household animals
Since mice, snakes, and similar animals also frequently traverse the house (share the 'illa), the ruling of purity is extended to them via qiyas jali (obvious analogy).
The asl (original case) is the cat; the far' (new case) is each household pest.
4
Understand the ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school
While the basic purity is agreed, there is disagreement on whether the cat's su'r is makruh. Al-Karkhi's view (makruh tanzihan) is preferred over al-Tahawi's (makruh tahriman).
The preferred view is al-ashah, chosen for its alignment with the hadith and athar.
5
Compare with other madhahib
Most other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) hold that the cat's su'r is not disliked at all. Note the thamarah al-khilaf in practice.
The practical difference: avoiding or not avoiding the cat's leftover water.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في القياس الشرعي. الهرة. فقال علي رضي الله عنه: «الهرة ليست بنجسة، فإنها من الطوافين عليكم والطوافات». فقاس أصحابنا جميع ما يسكن في البيوت كالفأرة والحية على الهرة بعلة الطواف. وبهذا يستدل على أن سؤرها ليس بنجس، وعليه كثير من الاعتماد، ولذا ذهب أبو يوسف والشافعي ومالك وأحمد والثوري والأوزاعي وإسحاق وأبو عبيد إلى أنه غير مكروه. وقيل: هو قول مالك وغيره من أهل المدينة، والليث وغيره من أهل مصر والأوزاعي وغيره من أهل الشام والثوري وغيره من أهل العراق، والشافعي وأصحابه وأحمد وإسحاق وأبي عبيد وعكرمة وإبراهيم وعطاء بن يسار والحسن كما قاله البر، واختاره الطحاوي من الحنفية، ورواية عن محمد أيضاً. لكن ما ذكره الطحاوي في «معاني الآثار» يدل على أنه مكروه تحريماً، واختار الكرخي من أصحابنا أنه مكروه تنزيهاً، وهو الأصح الأقرب إلى موافقة الأخبار والآثار. كذا في «الحصول». أخرجه مالك في الموطأ رقم ٤٢ باب الطهور للوضوء، وأحمد في مسنده رقم ٢٢٥٨١، وأبو داود في باب سؤر الهرة رقم ٧٥، والترمذي في باب ما جاء في سؤر الهرة رقم ۹٢ قال الترمذي: هذا حديث حسن صحيح، وابن ماجه في باب الوضوء بسؤر الهرة رقم ٣٦٧، والدارمي في باب الهرة إذا ولغت في الإناء، وصحيح ابن حبان ٤/١١٥ عن كبشة بنت كعب بن مالك الهلال المهن.
Section on legal analogy. The cat. Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'The cat is not impure, for it is one of those that go around you and those that go around.' So our scholars analogized all that dwell in houses, such as the mouse and the snake, to the cat on the basis of the cause of going around. And by this it is deduced that its leftover water is not impure, and much reliance is placed on this. For this reason, Abu Yusuf, al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad, al-Thawri, al-Awza'i, Ishaq, and Abu Ubayd went that it is not disliked. And it is said: it is the view of Malik and others from the people of Madinah, al-Layth and others from the people of Egypt, al-Awza'i and others from the people of Sham, al-Thawri and others from the people of Iraq, al-Shafi'i and his companions, Ahmad, Ishaq, Abu Ubayd, Ikrimah, Ibrahim, Ata ibn Yasar, and al-Hasan as reported by al-Barr, and al-Tahawi from the Hanafis chose it, and it is also a narration from Muhammad. However, what al-Tahawi mentioned in Ma'ani al-Athar indicates that it is prohibitively disliked, and al-Karkhi from our companions chose that it is lightly disliked, and it is the most correct and closest to agreement with the reports and traditions. As stated in al-Husul. It was narrated by Malik in al-Muwatta no. 42, chapter of purification for wudu, and Ahmad in his Musnad no. 22581, and Abu Dawud in the chapter of the cat's leftover water no. 75, and al-Tirmidhi in the chapter of the cat's leftover water no. 92, al-Tirmidhi said: this hadith is hasan sahih, and Ibn Majah in the chapter of wudu with the cat's leftover water no. 367, and al-Darimi in the chapter of the cat if it drinks from a vessel, and Sahih Ibn Hibban 4/115 from Kabshah bint Ka'b ibn Malik al-Hilali al-Muhann.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is a classic example of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul. The text begins by stating the section on qiyas. Then it presents a hadith from Imam Ali (RA) that the cat is not impure because it frequents households. The Hanafi scholars (أصحابنا) use this hadith to extend the ruling of purity to other household pests like mice and snakes, by identifying the 'illa (cause) as 'tawwaf' (going around/traversing) — meaning these animals frequently move around in homes. This is qiyas jali (obvious analogy). The legal effect is that the water left over (su'r) from these animals is pure (not najis). Then the text discusses the ikhtilaf: most scholars (including Abu Yusuf, Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad) hold that the cat's su'r is not even disliked (ghayr makruh). However, within the Hanafi school, there is a difference: al-Tahawi reported that it is makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked), but al-Karkhi said it is makruh tanzihan (lightly disliked), and the latter is considered the preferred view (al-ashah) because it aligns better with the hadith and athar. The footnote provides the chain of the hadith from various sources. This passage demonstrates how qiyas operates in Hanafi fiqh and the importance of 'illa.

Key Terms
السؤر (al-su'r): The water left over after an animal drinks.
الطواف (al-tawwaf): Frequent movement and going around in the house.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view (al-ashah) on the cat's su'r, what is the ruling?
A) Pure and not disliked at all
B) Pure but lightly disliked (makruh tanzihan)
C) Pure but prohibitively disliked (makruh tahriman)
D) Impure (najis)

Key Takeaway
The cat's su'r is pure, and by qiyas on the 'illa of tawwaf, the same ruling applies to other household animals, with a preferred Hanafi view of light dislike.

Extracting 'illa from Sunnah: Qiyas on Sleep and Wudu
Extracting 'illa and qiyās with inter-madhhab ikhtilāf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract the effective cause ('illa) from a hadith using taḥqīq al-manāt, apply qiyās jaliyy to extend the ruling to analogous cases, and identify the points of ikhtilāf among madhāhib regarding wudū’ after sleep.

Core Idea
The 'illa for wudū’ after sleep is joint relaxation (istirkhā’ al-mafāṣil); qiyās extends the ruling only where relaxation occurs.

This passage from Uṣūl al-Shāshī demonstrates how a ruling is derived from the Sunnah by first identifying the explicit cause from a hadith and then applying qiyās to new scenarios. The Prophet's statement explicitly negates wudū’ for certain sleep positions and affirms it for lying down, with a causal link to joint relaxation. Through linguistic analysis of the words 'fa' and 'inna, the 'illa is confirmed, allowing extension to positions like leaning. The passage also records a rich ikhtilāf among schools, illustrating how different approaches to the 'illa lead to different rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source text and its ruling
Locate the hadith cited in the passage. Note that it distinguishes between positions that require wudū’ (lying down) and those that do not (standing, sitting, bowing, prostrating). The ruling is explicit: wudū’ is only for the one who sleeps lying down.
The hadith is the primary dalīl from the Sunnah.
2
Extract the 'illa through taḥqīq al-manāt
The hadith itself provides the cause: 'for when he sleeps lying down, his joints relax.' This phrase (فإنه إذا نام مضطجعاً استرخت مفاصله) indicates that the relaxation of joints (istirkhā’ al-mafāṣil) is the effective cause. The fa' and 'inna are linguistic markers of causality.
This is a clear example of tahqīq al-manāt where the 'illa is explicitly stated.
3
Understand the linguistic indicators of causality
The passage explains that the fa' in 'fa innahu' and the word 'inna are used to indicate causality, similar to other Arabic usages. This linguistic analysis confirms that the relaxation is the cause, not a mere description.
This step is crucial for usul al-fiqh methodology.
4
Apply qiyās jaliyy to analogous cases
Once the 'illa is established, qiyās is applied to positions where joint relaxation also occurs, such as sleeping leaning or resting on something. The ruling (absence of wudū’) is extended from lying down to these positions because the 'illa is present.
Qiyās jaliyy is used because the 'illa is clear and the analogy is direct.
5
Map the inter-madhhab ikhtilāf
The text reports differences: Hanafis limit wudū’ to lying down or leaning; Shāfi‘īs require wudū’ for all sleep except sitting alone; Mālikīs require it for lying down and prostration but not sitting unless prolonged; etc. Each school's position stems from their interpretation of the 'illa and its scope.
Ikhtilāf here is legitimate, based on different uṣūl approaches.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومثال العلة المعلومة بالسنة في قوله عليه السلام: «ليس الوضوء على من نام قائماً أو قاعداً أو راكعاً أو ساجداً، إنما الوضوء على من نام مضطجعاً، فإنه إذا نام مضطجعاً استرخت مفاصله». جعل استرخاء المفاصل علةً فيتعدى الحكم بهذه العلة إلى النوم مستنداً أو متكئاً على شيء لو أُزيل عنه لسقط. ومن عم الاسترخاء علةً: لأن الفاء في قوله عليه السلام: «فإنه» إنما يذكر مثله للعلية في كلامهم كما يقال: «أبشر فقد أتاك الغوث»، وكذا كلمة «إن» تذكر لبيان العلة كما في قول الشاعر: بكر يا صاحبي قبل البحير إن ذاك النجاح في التبكير، ونحوها قوله جل جلاله: {وَلا تُخَاطِبْنِي فِي الَّذِينَ ظَلَمُوا إِنَّهُمْ مُغْرَقُونَ} [هود:37]. كذا في «المعدن» بزيادة. هذا القبيل قوله جل جلاله. فيتعدى الحكم إلخ: اختلف فيه الفقهاء، فقال الإمام مالك: من نام مضطجعاً أو ساجداً فليتوضأ، ومن نام جالساً فلا، إلا أن يطول نومه، وهو قول الزهري إمام المحدثين وربيعة، والأوزاعي وأحمد. وقال الإمام أبو حنيفة وأصحابه: لا وضوء إلا على من نام مضطجعاً أو متكئاً. وقال أبو يوسف: إن تعمد النوم في السجود فعليه الوضوء. وقال الثوري والحسن بن يحيى وحماد بن أبي سليمان والنخعي: أنه لا وضوء إلا على من اضطجع. وقال الشافعي: عليه على كل نائم الوضوء إلا الجالس وحده. وقال ابن القطان: أجمع العلماء على أن النوم القليل لا ينقض الوضوء إلا المزني من الشافعية، فإنه خرق الإجماع وجعل قليله حدثاً، وأجمعوا على نوم المضطجع ينقض الوضوء. والله أعلم. كذا في «الحصول». إلى النوم مستنداً إلخ: لا إلى النوم ساجداً؛ لما مر من الحديث نفياً صريحاً، ولما رواه البيهقي في «الخلافيات» عن أنس رضي الله عنه قال: إذا نام العبد في السجود يباهي الله تعالى ملائكته فيقول: انظروا إلى عبدي روحه عندي وجسده في طاعتي. كذا في «الحصول». أخرجه أبو داود في باب الوضوء من النوم، رقم: ۲۰۲، والترمذي في باب ما جاء في الوضوء من النوم، رقم: ۷۷، عن ابن عباس، وقال الهيثمي: ورجاله موثقون. [مجمع الزوائد ١/٥٦٢، رقم: ١٢٨٧]
And an example of the cause known from the Sunnah is in his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is no wudu upon one who sleeps standing, or sitting, or bowing, or prostrating; wudu is only upon one who sleeps lying down, for when he sleeps lying down, his joints relax.' He made the relaxation of joints the cause, so the ruling extends by this cause to sleeping leaning or resting on something such that if it were removed he would fall. And he generalizes relaxation as the cause because the fa' in his statement 'for when he sleeps' is used as a marker of causality in their speech, as it is said: 'Rejoice, for help has come to you.' Similarly, the word 'inna' is used to explain the cause, as in the poet's saying: 'Hasten, O my friend, before the sea, for success lies in early rising,' and similar to it is His statement, may He be exalted: 'And do not address Me concerning those who have wronged; indeed, they are to be drowned.' As stated in al-Ma'din with addition. This category includes His statement. 'So the ruling extends' etc.: The jurists differed. Imam Malik said: Whoever sleeps lying down or prostrating must perform wudu, and whoever sleeps sitting does not, unless his sleep is long — this is the opinion of al-Zuhri, the imam of hadith scholars, and Rabi'a, al-Awza'i, and Ahmad. Imam Abu Hanifa and his companions said: No wudu except upon one who sleeps lying down or leaning. Abu Yusuf said: If he intentionally sleeps in prostration, then wudu is required. Al-Thawri, al-Hasan ibn Yahya, Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman, and al-Nakha'i said: No wudu except on one who lies down. Al-Shafi'i said: Wudu is required for every sleeper except the sitting one alone. Ibn al-Qattan said: The scholars are unanimous that light sleep does not break wudu except al-Muzani from the Shafi'is, for he broke the consensus and considered even light sleep as hadath; and they are unanimous that the sleep of the one lying down breaks wudu. And Allah knows best. As stated in al-Husul. 'To sleeping leaning etc.': not to sleeping in prostration; because of the hadith mentioned that explicitly negates it, and because of what al-Bayhaqi narrated in al-Khilafiyyat from Anas (may Allah be pleased with him): When the servant sleeps in prostration, Allah boasts to His angels saying: Look at My servant, his soul is with Me and his body is in My obedience. As stated in al-Husul. It was narrated by Abu Dawud in the chapter of wudu from sleep, no. 202, and al-Tirmidhi in the chapter of wudu from sleep, no. 77, from Ibn Abbas, and al-Haythami said: Its narrators are trustworthy. [Majma' al-Zawa'id 1/562, no. 1287]
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents the second example of an 'illa derived from the Sunnah. The hadith (attributed to the Prophet) states that wudu is only required when one sleeps lying down, because only then the joints relax (istirkha' al-mafasil). The 'illa is the relaxation of joints, which causes the limbs to loosen and wind to pass, breaking wudu. By qiyas, this ruling extends to any sleep position that leads to relaxation, such as leaning or resting against something so that if removed, the person would fall. The text then discusses the linguistic indicators of causality: the fa' and the word 'inna. Then the text reports a lengthy ikhtilaf among scholars about which sleep positions nullify wudu. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and his companions) is that only sleeping lying down or leaning breaks wudu; sitting or standing does not. Abu Yusuf adds that intentional sleep in prostration also breaks. The text also mentions the hadith about the virtue of sleeping in prostration, which indicates it does not break wudu. This example demonstrates how qiyas operates with an explicit 'illa from hadith, and how different schools apply it.

Key Terms
استرخاء المفاصل (istirkha' al-mafasil): Relaxation of joints; the 'illa for wudu after sleep.
علة ('illa): The effective cause in qiyas that determines the ruling.
قياس جلي (qiyas jaliy): Clear analogy where the 'illa is explicitly stated in the primary text and applies directly to the new case.
تحقيق المناط (tahqiq al-manat): Verification of the effective cause; confirming that the 'illa is present in the new case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, which sleep position requires wudu?
A) Sitting
B) Standing
C) Lying down or leaning
D) Prostrating

Key Takeaway
The effective cause (ʻilla) for wudū’ after sleep is joint relaxation, and qiyās extends the ruling only where this cause is present.

How Illah is Known from the Sunnah: The Case of Sleep and Wudu
Exemplifies illah from Sunnah with hadith on sleep and wudu, then records inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the linguistic indicators (fa, inna) that reveal the illah in a Prophetic hadith, extract the illah of relaxation of joints, and apply it to analogous cases like reclining sleep, while evaluating the Hanafi position against other schools.

Core Idea
The illah (relaxation of joints) is derived from the hadith's explicit causal link (fa) and explanation (inna), limiting wudu to lying down sleep and its analogies.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi demonstrates how a legal cause (illah) is known from the Sunnah by analyzing a hadith on sleep and wudu. The Prophet (SAW) explicitly linked wudu to the relaxation of joints when lying down, using the particles 'fa' and 'inna' to indicate causality and explanation. This allows the Hanafi school to extend the ruling to reclining sleep while excluding prostration. The passage then records the detailed inter-madhhab dispute, showcasing how different schools interpret the same hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its structure
The hadith negates wudu for standing, sitting, bowing, prostrating sleep, and affirms it for lying down, with the explanation 'for when he sleeps lying down, his joints relax.'
The negation and affirmation set up the scope of the ruling.
2
Extract the illah (effective cause)
The explicit statement 'his joints relax' after 'fa' indicates the cause. The Hanafi school identifies relaxation of joints as the illah.
The particle 'fa' is key for causality in Arabic.
3
Extend the ruling by analogy (qiyas)
The illah of relaxation applies to reclining sleep (if support removed, person falls). Not to prostration because the hadith explicitly negates it and there is a virtue narration.
Analogical extension requires the same illah.
4
Compare the Hanafi position with other schools
Record the positions of Malik, Shafi'i, etc., and their reasons.
Malik includes prostration; Shafi'i includes all except sitting alone.
5
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequences: Hanafi: no wudu for prostration sleep; Maliki: yes; Shafi'i: all except sitting.
The difference affects daily practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومثال العلة المعلومة بالسنة في قوله عليه: "ليس الوضوء على من نام قائماً أو قاعداً أو راكعاً أو ساجداً، إنما الوضوء على من نام مضطجعًا، فإنه إذا نام مضطجعاً استرخت مفاصله" * جَعَل استرخاء المفاصل علةً فيتعدى الحكم بهذه العلة إلى النوم مستنداً أو متكنًا إلى شيء لو أُزِيلَ عنه لسقط. ومن عم الاسترخاء علةً: لأن الفاء في قوله عليه: "فإنه" إنما يذكر مثله للعلية في كلامهم كما يقال: "أبشر فقد أتاك الغوث"، وكذا كلمة "إن" يذكر لبيان كما في قول الشاعر: بكر يا صاحبي قبل البحير إن ذاك النجاح في التبكير، ونحو قوله جل جلاله: ﴿وَلا تُخَاطِبْنِي فِي الَّذِينَ ظَلَمُوا إِنَّهُمْ مُغْرَقُونَ﴾ كذا في "المعدن" بزيادة. هذا القبيل : اختلف فيه الفقهاء، فقال الإمام مالك : من نام مضطجعاً أو ساجداً فليتوضأ، ومن نام جالساً فلا، إلا أن يطول نومه، وهو قول الزهري إمام المحدثين وربيعة، والأوزاعي وأحمد، وقال الإمام أبو حنيفة وأصحابه: لا وضوء إلا على من نام مضطجعاً أو متكياً، وقال أبو يوسف: إن تعمد النوم في السجود فعليه الوضوء، وقال الثوري والحسن بن يحي وحماد بن أبي سليمان والنخعي أنه لا وضوء إلا على من اضطجع، وقال الشافعي له على كل نائم الوضوء إلا الجالس وحده، وقال ابن القطان: أجمع العلماء على أن النوم القليل لا ينقض الوضوء إلا المزني من الشافعية، فإنه خرق الإجماع وجعل قليله حدثاً، وأجمعوا على نوم المضطجع ينقض الوضوء والله أعلم كذا في "الحصول". إلى النوم مستنداً إلخ: لا إلى النوم ساجداً؛ لما مر من الحديث نفياً صريحاً، ولما رواه البيهقي في "الخلافيات" عن أنس له إذا نام العبد في السجود يباهي الله تعالى ملائكته فيقول : انظروا إلى عبدي روحه عندي وجسده في طاعتي كذا في "الحصول". * أخرجه أبو داود في باب الوضوء من النوم، رقم: ۲۰۲ ، والترمذي في باب ما جاء في الوضوء من النوم، رقم: ۷۷، عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما، وقال الهيثمي : ورجاله موثقون. [مجمع الزوائد ٥٦٢/١، رقم: ١٢٨٧]
An example of the cause known from the Sunnah is in his saying (peace be upon him): 'There is no wudu on one who slept standing, or sitting, or bowing, or prostrating; wudu is only on one who slept lying down, for when he sleeps lying down, his joints relax.' So he made the relaxation of joints a cause, and the ruling is extended by this cause to sleeping leaning or propping against something such that if it were removed he would fall. And some generalised relaxation as the cause because the 'fa' (so) in his saying 'for when' is only mentioned for causality in their speech, as is said: 'Rejoice, for help has come to you.' Similarly the word 'inna' is mentioned for explanation, as in the poet's saying: 'Hasten O my companion before the sea, for that success is in early rising,' and similar to His exalted saying: 'And do not address Me concerning those who have wronged; indeed, they are to be drowned.' Thus in al-Ma'din with additions. Concerning this category: the jurists differed. Imam Malik said: Whoever sleeps lying down or prostrating must perform wudu; if he sleeps sitting, then no, unless his sleep is long. This is also the saying of al-Zuhri, Imam of the hadith scholars, Rabi'ah, al-Awza'i, and Ahmad. Imam Abu Hanifa and his companions said: No wudu except on one who sleeps lying down or reclining. Abu Yusuf said: If he intentionally sleeps in prostration, he must perform wudu. Al-Thawri, al-Hasan ibn Yahya, Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman, and al-Nakha'i said: No wudu except on one who lies down. Al-Shafi'i said: Every sleeper must perform wudu except the one sitting alone. Ibn al-Qattan said: The scholars are agreed that a little sleep does not break wudu, except al-Muzani among the Shafi'is, for he broke consensus and made a little of it an impurity; and they agreed that the sleep of one lying down breaks wudu. And Allah knows best. Thus in al-Husul. 'to sleeping leaning etc.': not to sleeping prostrating, because of the explicit negation in the hadith mentioned, and because of what al-Bayhaqi narrated in al-Khilafiyyat from Anas (may Allah be pleased with him) that when a slave sleeps in prostration, Allah boasts to His angels saying: Look at My slave, his soul is with Me and his body is in My obedience. Thus in al-Husul. * Narrated by Abu Dawud in the chapter of wudu from sleep, no. 202, and al-Tirmidhi in the chapter on wudu from sleep, no. 77, from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both), and al-Haythami said: Its narrators are trustworthy. [Majma' al-Zawa'id 1/562, no. 1287]
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of how a legal cause (illah) is known from the Sunnah and then used to extend the ruling to other cases. The author gives an example from a hadith regarding wudu after sleep. The Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly stated that wudu is required only for one who sleeps lying down, because in that position the joints relax, whereas in standing, sitting, bowing, or prostrating, the joints remain tense. The author explains that the particle 'fa' (so) in the hadith indicates causality, and the word 'inna' is used to clarify the reason, similar to Qur'anic usage. Then he records a detailed inter-madhhab dispute: Imam Malik and others require wudu for lying down and prostrating sleep, but not for sitting unless prolonged; Abu Hanifa and his companions include reclining; Abu Yusuf adds intentional sleep in prostration; al-Shafi'i requires wudu for all except sitting alone. The author also notes a consensus that a little sleep does not break wudu (except al-Muzani's minority view) and that lying-down sleep does break wudu. Finally, he clarifies that the extension to leaning sleep is valid, but not to prostrating sleep because the hadith explicitly negates it, and also a narration mentions that Allah praises the one who sleeps in prostration. This showcases how an illah from a specific text is extracted and applied analogically.

Key Terms
العلة (al-illah): The effective cause or attribute that justifies a legal ruling and allows analogical extension (qiyas).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which linguistic particle in the hadith indicates causality?
A) إنما
B) فإنه
C) ليس
D) على

Key Takeaway
The extraction of the illah from the Sunnah relies on textual indicators like 'fa' and 'inna', enabling analogical extension while respecting textual limits.

Transfer of Causal Efficacy Across Time and Condition at the Last Part
Explains transfer of causality and condition at last part

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that the cause for prayer obligation transfers across time segments and that the person's condition at the last segment determines the obligation.

Core Idea
The last part of prayer time fixes the obligation; a change there triggers or drops it.

This lesson explores how the obligation of prayer is linked to time in Hanafi usul. The cause (sabab) is the time itself, but it transfers across parts until the last part, where the obligation crystallizes. At that moment, the person's condition (adulthood, Islam, purity, travel, sanity) is decisive. We also see how continuous insanity beyond a day and night drops the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time parts
Understand that time is considered as a continuum of parts (ajza'). The first part is the earliest legally recognized moment.
The 'first part' may be absolute or relative, as explained in the text.
2
Track the transfer of causality
If prayer is not performed in the first part, the cause transfers to the next part, and so on until the last part where the obligation becomes established.
This transfer occurs automatically unless the prayer is performed earlier.
3
Consider the condition at the last part
The obligation is determined by the person's state (e.g., child/adult, disbeliever/Muslim, menstruating/pure, traveler/resident) at the last part of the time.
If the person becomes qualified at the last moment, the prayer becomes obligatory even if they were unqualified earlier.
4
Apply the rule to examples
Review the examples given: a child becoming adult, a disbeliever embracing Islam, a menstruating woman becoming pure, a traveler becoming resident at the last part — all trigger obligation.
Conversely, if insanity or unconsciousness occurs continuously exceeding a day and night, the obligation drops.
5
Note the exception for insanity
Only continuous insanity extending beyond a day and night drops the prayer; brief or intermittent episodes do not.
This is a specific Hanafi threshold.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أسباب الأحكام الشرعية ثم بعد ذلك طريقان: أحدهما: نقل السبية من الجزء الأول إلى الثاني إذا لم يؤد في الجزء الأول، ثم إلى الثالث والرابع إلى أن ينتهي إلى آخر الوقت، فيتقرر الوجوب حينئذ، ويُعتبر حال العبد في ذلك الجزء، ويعتبر صفة ذلك الجزء. عند الشرع إلى آخر الوقت الآخر من أجزاء الوقت وبيان اعتبار حال العبد فيه: أنه لو كان صبيا في أول الوقت بالغاً في ذلك الجزء، من الأهلية وعدمها الآخر من الوقت أو كان كافراً في أول الوقت مسلماً في ذلك الجزء أو كانت حائضاً أو نُفَساءَ في أول الوقت طاهرةً في ذلك الجزء وجبت الصلاة. وعلى هذا جميع صور حدوث الأهلية في آخر الوقت. ثم بعد ذلك: أي بعد أن يثبت أن الجزء الأول سبب للوجوب لابد أن يعلم كيف يكون باقي أجزاء الوقت وله طريقان كما بين في الكتاب. ثم إلى الثالث إلخ: أي ثم إن لم يؤد في الجزء الثاني، انتقلت السببية منه إلى الجزء الثالث، وإن لم يؤد في الجزء الثالث انتقلت من إلى الجزء الرابع الذي يلي الثالث، وكذا تنتقل السببية من جزء إلى جزء إلى أن ينتهي إلخ. [عمدة الحواشي: ص ٢٣٠] الناقص ذلك الجزء إلخ: أي يعتبر حال ذلك الموجب للصلاة بنفس الوجوب كمالاً ونقصاناً، فإن كان كاملاً وجبت كاملة، فإن الوجوب مضاف إلى العلة فبكماله يكمل وبنقصه ينقص، فلو أديت كاملة أيضاً صحت، وإلا فسدت، وإن كان ناقصاً وجبت ناقصة فلو أديت كاملة صحت أيضاً؛ لأن الضروري أن لا ينقص الأداء عن قدر الوجوب كما إذا أدى العصر أي قضاه بعد الوقت؛ لأن سبب وجوبها مجموع الوقت وهو مشتمل على أيضاً، ومجموع الكامل والناقص ناقص من وجه وإن لم يكن ناقصاً كاملاً، فهو أيضاً كامل من وجه باعتبار أكثر أجزائه لجهة الكمال فيه راجحة وبهذا قارب الأداء فارق الوجوب ومساواته، ولذا لا يصح قضاؤه في الوقت الناقص كأوقات الطلوع والغروب والظهيرة؛ لأن الوجوب من وجه كامل أيضاً بل بعامة أجزائه، وللأكثر حكم الكل فلا يؤدي به الناقص الممتحض النقص كذا في "الحصول". في أول الوقت إلخ أي في جزء أول مقدم على سائر أجزائه غير مسبوق بجزء آخر منه وهو الأول الحقيقي، أو في جزء أول مقدم على الأخير من أجزائه، أو على بعض أجزائه، وإلا كان من الأوساط وهو الأول الإضافي، وهو أعم من الأول والأول أولى بالنظر إلى اللفظ ، والثاني بالنظر إلى محل الكلام مما يسبق كذا في "الفصول". وعلى العكس بأن يحدث حيض أو أنفاس أو جنون مستوعب أو إغماء ممتد في ذلك الجزء سقطت عنه الصلاة. ولو كان مسافراً في أول الوقت مقيماً في آخره يصلي أربعاً، ولو كان مقيماً في أول الوقت مسافراً في آخره يصلي ركعتين. وبيان اعتبار صفة ذلك الجزء أن ذلك الجزء إن كان كاملاً تقررت الوظيفة كاملة، فلا الآخر من الوقت يخرج عن العُهدة بأدائها في الأوقات المكروهة. يثبت الواجب كاملاً وجبت أو جنون مستوعب إلخ قيد الجنون والإغماء بالاستيعاب والامتداد؛ لأجل أن غير المستوعب وغير الممتد لا تسقط به الصلاة. [عمدة الحواشي : ص ۲۳۱] والمراد بالاستيعاب والامتداد ما يزيد على يوم وليلة. [حاشية الشيخ أكرم الندوي: ص ٢٥٣] فلا يخرج إلخ لأن ما وجب كاملاً لا يتأدى بصفة النقصان، كالصوم المنذور المطلق لا يتأدى في أيام النحر والتشريق وكالسجدة إذا قرأها نازلاً فركب سجد بالإيماء لا يتأدى؛ لأنها كاملة فلا تتأدى ناقصة كذا قيل. بأدائها في الأوقات ويعارضه ما رواه الشيخان عن أبي هريرة الله رفعه "من" أدرك ركعة قبل أن تغرب الشمس فقد أدرك العصر ، وأجاب عنه الحنفية له بأن هذا الحديث عارضه أحاديث كثيرة متواترة المعنى منها: ما أخرجه البخاري ومسلم عن الخدري الله رفعه: "لا صلاة بعد الصبح حتى تطلع الشمس، ولا صلاة بعد العصر حتى تغيب الشمس"، ومنها ما رواه مسلم عن عقبة بن عامر ما رفعه: "كان ينهانا أن نصلي فيهن، وأن نقبر فيهن موتانا حين تطلع الشمس بازغة حتى ترتفع، وحين تقوم قائم الظهيرة حتى تزول الشمس، وحين تتضيف الشمس"، فإذا تعارضا فالواجب حينئذ كما ثبت في الأصول هو المصير إلى القياس، والقياس قد رجح حديث الصحة في العصر، وحديث الفساد في الفجر، فعلمنا بهذا النمط هكذا في "الهداية" و"شرح الوقاية" وحواشيها ، ثم الطحاوي قد أطال فيه الكلام وحقق المقام دراية كما هو شأنه ودأبه في "شرح معاني الآثار"، وخص الشافعية أحاديث النهي بالنوافل لا بالفرائض، قلنا: بلا مخصص فلا يسمع كيف والنكرة في سياق النفي تفيد العموم قطعاً، وما قيل: لا تعارض بين هذين الحديثين؛ لأن المقصود بالنهي هو النهي عن بداية الصلاة، وفي الحديث صحة الإتمام والقياس فاسد بإزاء النص، قلنا: هذا كلام لسفيه؛ لأن القياس إنما صرنا إليه= هو
Chapter on the causes of legal rulings. Then after that, two ways: one: the transfer of causality from the first part to the second if he did not perform in the first part, then to the third and fourth until it reaches the last time, then the obligation is established at that time, and the condition of the servant is considered in that part, and the quality of that part is considered. According to the Sharia, until the last time, the last of the parts of time, and an explanation of considering the condition of the servant in it: that if he was a child at the beginning of the time, an adult in that part, from capability or lack thereof, or was a disbeliever at the beginning of the time, a Muslim in that part, or was menstruating or postpartum at the beginning of the time, pure in that part, the prayer becomes obligatory. And upon this are all cases of capability occurring at the last time. Then after that: after it is proven that the first part is a cause for obligation, it is necessary to know how the remaining parts of time are, and it has two ways as explained in the book. Then to the third etc.: meaning if he did not perform in the second part, causality transfers from it to the third part, and if he did not perform in the third part, it transfers to the fourth part which comes after the third, and so causality transfers from part to part until it ends etc. [Umdat al-Hawashi: p. 230] The deficient that part etc.: meaning the condition of the one obligated for prayer is considered in terms of completeness and deficiency, so if he is complete, a complete obligation is required, because the obligation is attributed to the cause, so by its completeness it is complete, and by its deficiency it is deficient. If it is performed as complete, it is valid, otherwise it is invalid. And if it is deficient, a deficient obligation is required, so if he performs it as complete, it is also valid; because essentially the performance should not fall short of the level of obligation, as when he performs Asr after its time; because the cause of its obligation is the entire time which includes also, and the combination of complete and deficient is deficient in some respect, even if it is not completely deficient, it is also complete in some respect considering most of its parts, and the aspect of completeness is preponderant, and by this it approaches performance, differing from obligation and its equality, and therefore its qada is not valid in deficient times like the times of sunrise, sunset, and zenith; because the obligation in some respect is also complete, indeed with all its parts, and the majority has the ruling of the whole, so the purely deficient is not performed with it. So in "al-Husul". At the beginning of the time etc.: meaning in a first part that precedes all its other parts, not preceded by another part from it, and it is the real first, or in a first part that is before the last of its parts, or before some of its parts, otherwise it is from the middle, and it is the relative first, and it is more general than the first, and the first is more appropriate with regard to the wording, and the second with regard to the context of the speech what precedes so in "al-Fusul". And conversely, if menstruation, postpartum, continuous insanity, or prolonged unconsciousness occurs in that part, the prayer is dropped. And if he was a traveler at the beginning of the time and resident at its end, he prays four; and if he was resident at the beginning and traveler at the end, he prays two rak'ahs. And explanation of considering the quality of that part: that if that part is complete, the function is established as complete, so he does not discharge the responsibility by performing it in disliked times. The obligation is established as complete. It is obligatory. Or continuous insanity etc.: the restriction of insanity and unconsciousness to continuity and prolongation; because that which is not continuous and not prolonged does not drop the prayer. [Umdat al-Hawashi: p. 231] And what is meant by continuity and prolongation is what exceeds a day and a night. [Hashiyat Shaykh Akram al-Nadwi: p. 253] So he does not discharge etc. because what is obligatory as complete is not performed with the quality of deficiency, like an absolute vowed fast is not performed on the days of sacrifice and tashriq, and like the prostration if he recited it while descending, then rode, he prostrated with gestures, it is not performed; because it is complete, so it is not performed deficiently, so it is said. By performing it in the times, and it is contradicted by what the two Shaykhs narrated from Abu Hurayra, may Allah be pleased with him, raised: "Whoever catches a rak'ah before the sun sets has caught Asr." The Hanafis responded to him by saying that this hadith is contradicted by many hadiths with mutawatir meaning, including what al-Bukhari and Muslim transmitted from al-Khudri, may Allah be pleased with him, raised: "No prayer after Fajr until the sun rises, and no prayer after Asr until the sun sets," and including what Muslim transmitted from Uqba ibn Amir, may Allah be pleased with him, raised: "He used to forbid us from praying in them, and from burying our dead in them, when the sun rises rising until it rises high, and when the sun stands at zenith until it declines, and when the sun inclines." When they conflict, then the obligation at that time, as established in principles, is to resort to analogy, and analogy has given preponderance to the hadith of validity for Asr, and the hadith of invalidity for Fajr. Thus we know by this pattern, so in "al-Hidaya" and "Sharh al-Wiqaya" and their footnotes, then al-Tahawi has spoken at length and investigated the matter expertly as is his manner and practice in "Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar." The Shafi'is specified the hadiths of prohibition to supererogatory prayers, not obligatory. We say: without a specifier, it is not heard, and how, while the indefinite in the context of negation indicates absolute generality. And what is said: there is no conflict between these two hadiths because the intended meaning of the prohibition is the prohibition of beginning the prayer, and in the hadith the validity of completing it, and analogy is invalid against the text. We say: this is the speech of a foolish person; because analogy we have resorted to...
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the usul rule regarding how the cause (sabab) for prayer obligation transfers across the parts of the time period. The commentator explains that the causality starts from the first part and, if the prayer is not performed, transfers to subsequent parts until the last part, at which point the obligation becomes established. At that moment, the condition of the person (i.e., whether they have attained puberty, are Muslim, are pure) is considered. If someone was a child, disbeliever, or menstruating at the first part but becomes adult, Muslim, or pure at the last part, the prayer becomes obligatory. Conversely, if they become insane or unconscious continuously for more than a day and night, the prayer drops. The quality of that last part is also considered: if it is complete (not a deficient time like sunrise, sunset, or zenith), the obligation is complete and must be performed fully; performing it in those disliked times does not fulfill the obligation. The text then addresses a hadith conflict: the hadith 'Whoever catches a rak'ah before sunset has caught Asr' seems to allow prayer at sunset, but it is countered by many hadiths prohibiting prayer at those times. The Hanafis resolve this by resorting to analogy (qiyas), which weighs the prohibition for Fajr as invalid and for Asr as valid. The Shafi'is argue the prohibition is only for voluntary prayers, but the Hanafis rebut that the general negation implies generality, and the claim of no conflict is rejected because the analogy is necessary. The passage ends mid-sentence, likely continuing in the next page.

Key Terms
السببية (al-sababiyya): The causal efficacy that transfers across parts of time for prayer obligation.
الجزء الأخير (al-juz' al-akhir): The last part of the prayer time when the obligation becomes established.
الاستيعاب والامتداد (al-isti'ab wa al-imtidad): Continuity and prolongation of insanity or unconsciousness exceeding a day and night, which drops the prayer obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person is a traveler at the beginning of Zuhr time and becomes resident at the last part, how many rak'ahs must he pray?
A) Two rak'ahs
B) Four rak'ahs
C) Two rak'ahs if he intended travel
D) He is not obligated

Key Takeaway
The last part of prayer time is decisive for obligation; changes in condition at that moment trigger or abolish the duty.

Al-Sunnah as Source
advanced
10 min
The Quality of Time and the Hadith Conflict: Obligatory Prayers in Disliked Times
Explains quality of time and resolves hadith conflict via qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on performing obligatory prayers in disliked times and apply the usul method of resolving conflicting hadiths through analogy (qiyas).

Core Idea
A complete obligation cannot be fulfilled in a deficient time; conflicting hadiths are resolved by qiyas, which permits Asr but not Fajr in disliked times.

The second major point of this passage concerns the quality of the time part. A complete obligation (wajib kamil) cannot be discharged in a deficient time such as sunrise, sunset, or zenith. The text then confronts a hadith conflict: the prohibition of prayer at these times versus the hadith 'Whoever catches a rak'ah before sunset has caught Asr.' The Hanafis resolve this by resorting to analogy (qiyas), allowing Asr but invalidating Fajr. This lesson unpacks that usul process.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of complete vs deficient time
If the last part of time is complete (not a deficient time like sunrise, sunset, or zenith), the obligation is complete and cannot be performed in a deficient time.
A deficient time is one in which prayer is normally disliked (makruh).
2
Identify the hadith conflict
The prohibition hadiths (mutawatir in meaning) forbid prayer at certain times, while the 'rak'ah' hadith indicates that catching a rak'ah before sunset counts as having prayed Asr.
Both sets of hadiths are authentic; the conflict is in their apparent application to obligatory prayers.
3
Apply the usul principle of ta'arud and tarjih
When hadiths conflict, the Hanafi method is to resort to analogy (qiyas) to weigh which evidence is stronger.
This is a standard usul principle when texts cannot be reconciled directly.
4
See how qiyas differentiates Asr from Fajr
Analogy gives preponderance to the hadith of validity for Asr (since its time can be extended by necessity) and to the prohibition for Fajr (since its time is short and the prohibition is stronger).
Thus, Asr prayed at sunset with at least one rak'ah before sunset is valid; Fajr at sunrise is invalid.
5
Evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument
Shafi'is restrict the prohibition to voluntary prayers only. Hanafis rebut by pointing out that the negation (لا صلاة) is general and includes obligatory prayers.
The indefinite in the context of negation indicates absolute generality (عموم) in Hanafi usul.

فصل في أسباب الأحكام الشرعية ثم بعد ذلك طريقان: أحدهما: نقل السبية من الجزء الأول إلى الثاني إذا لم يؤد في الجزء الأول، ثم إلى الثالث والرابع إلى أن ينتهي إلى آخر الوقت، فيتقرر الوجوب حينئذ، ويُعتبر حال العبد في ذلك الجزء، ويعتبر صفة ذلك الجزء. عند الشرع إلى آخر الوقت الآخر من أجزاء الوقت وبيان اعتبار حال العبد فيه: أنه لو كان صبيا في أول الوقت بالغاً في ذلك الجزء، من الأهلية وعدمها الآخر من الوقت أو كان كافراً في أول الوقت مسلماً في ذلك الجزء أو كانت حائضاً أو نُفَساءَ في أول الوقت طاهرةً في ذلك الجزء وجبت الصلاة. وعلى هذا جميع صور حدوث الأهلية في آخر الوقت. ثم بعد ذلك: أي بعد أن يثبت أن الجزء الأول سبب للوجوب لابد أن يعلم كيف يكون باقي أجزاء الوقت وله طريقان كما بين في الكتاب. ثم إلى الثالث إلخ: أي ثم إن لم يؤد في الجزء الثاني، انتقلت السببية منه إلى الجزء الثالث، وإن لم يؤد في الجزء الثالث انتقلت من إلى الجزء الرابع الذي يلي الثالث، وكذا تنتقل السببية من جزء إلى جزء إلى أن ينتهي إلخ. Then to the third etc.: meaning if he did not perform in the second part, causality transfers from it to the third part, and if he did not perform in the third part, it transfers to the fourth part which comes after the third, and so causality transfers from part to part until it ends etc. [Umdat al-Hawashi: p. 230] The deficient that part etc.: meaning the condition of the one obligated for prayer is considered in terms of completeness and deficiency, so if he is complete, a complete obligation is required, because the obligation is attributed to the cause, so by its completeness it is complete, and by its deficiency it is deficient. If it is performed as complete, it is valid, otherwise it is invalid. And if it is deficient, a deficient obligation is required, so if he performs it as complete, it is also valid; because essentially the performance should not fall short of the level of obligation, as when he performs Asr after its time; because the cause of its obligation is the entire time which includes also, and the combination of complete and deficient is deficient in some respect, even if it is not completely deficient, it is also complete in some respect considering most of its parts, and the aspect of completeness is preponderant, and by this it approaches performance, differing from obligation and its equality, and therefore its qada is not valid in deficient times like the times of sunrise, sunset, and zenith; because the obligation in some respect is also complete, indeed with all its parts, and the majority has the ruling of the whole, so the purely deficient is not performed with it. So in "al-Husul". At the beginning of the time etc.: meaning in a first part that precedes all its other parts, not preceded by another part from it, and it is the real first, or in a first part that is before the last of its parts, or before some of its parts, otherwise it is from the middle, and it is the relative first, and it is more general than the first, and the first is more appropriate with regard to the wording, and the second with regard to the context of the speech what precedes so in "al-Fusul". And conversely, if menstruation, postpartum, continuous insanity, or prolonged unconsciousness occurs in that part, the prayer is dropped. And if he was a traveler at the beginning of the time and resident at its end, he prays four; and if he was resident at the beginning and traveler at the end, he prays two rak'ahs. And explanation of considering the quality of that part: that if that part is complete, the function is established as complete, so he does not discharge the responsibility by performing it in disliked times. The obligation is established as complete. It is obligatory. Or continuous insanity etc.: the restriction of insanity and unconsciousness to continuity and prolongation; because that which is not continuous and not prolonged does not drop the prayer. [Umdat al-Hawashi: p. 231] And what is meant by continuity and prolongation is what exceeds a day and a night. [Hashiyat Shaykh Akram al-Nadwi: p. 253] So he does not discharge etc. because what is obligatory as complete is not performed with the quality of deficiency, like an absolute vowed fast is not performed on the days of sacrifice and tashriq, and like the prostration if he recited it while descending, then rode, he prostrated with gestures, it is not performed; because it is complete, so it is not performed deficiently, so it is said. By performing it in the times, and it is contradicted by what the two Shaykhs narrated from Abu Hurayra, may Allah be pleased with him, raised: "Whoever catches a rak'ah before the sun sets has caught Asr." The Hanafis responded to him by saying that this hadith is contradicted by many hadiths with mutawatir meaning, including what al-Bukhari and Muslim transmitted from al-Khudri, may Allah be pleased with him, raised: "No prayer after Fajr until the sun rises, and no prayer after Asr until the sun sets," and including what Muslim transmitted from Uqba ibn Amir, may Allah be pleased with him, raised: "He used to forbid us from praying in them, and from burying our dead in them, when the sun rises rising until it rises high, and when the sun stands at zenith until it declines, and when the sun inclines." When they conflict, then the obligation at that time, as established in principles, is to resort to analogy, and analogy has given preponderance to the hadith of validity for Asr, and the hadith of invalidity for Fajr. Thus we know by this pattern, so in "al-Hidaya" and "Sharh al-Wiqaya" and their footnotes, then al-Tahawi has spoken at length and investigated the matter expertly as is his manner and practice in "Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar." The Shafi'is specified the hadiths of prohibition to supererogatory prayers, not obligatory. We say: without a specifier, it is not heard, and how, while the indefinite in the context of negation indicates absolute generality. And what is said: there is no conflict between these two hadiths because the intended meaning of the prohibition is the prohibition of beginning the prayer, and in the hadith the validity of completing it, and analogy is invalid against the text. We say: this is the speech of a foolish person; because analogy we have resorted to...
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the usul rule regarding how the cause (sabab) for prayer obligation transfers across the parts of the time period. The commentator explains that the causality starts from the first part and, if the prayer is not performed, transfers to subsequent parts until the last part, at which point the obligation becomes established. At that moment, the condition of the person (i.e., whether they have attained puberty, are Muslim, are pure) is considered. If someone was a child, disbeliever, or menstruating at the first part but becomes adult, Muslim, or pure at the last part, the prayer becomes obligatory. Conversely, if they become insane or unconscious continuously for more than a day and night, the prayer drops. The quality of that last part is also considered: if it is complete (not a deficient time like sunrise, sunset, or zenith), the obligation is complete and must be performed fully; performing it in those disliked times does not fulfill the obligation. The text then addresses a hadith conflict: the hadith 'Whoever catches a rak'ah before sunset has caught Asr' seems to allow prayer at sunset, but it is countered by many hadiths prohibiting prayer at those times. The Hanafis resolve this by resorting to analogy (qiyas), which weighs the prohibition for Fajr as invalid and for Asr as valid. The Shafi'is argue the prohibition is only for voluntary prayers, but the Hanafis rebut that the general negation implies generality, and the claim of no conflict is rejected because the analogy is necessary. The passage ends mid-sentence, likely continuing in the next page.

Key Terms
السببية (al-sababiyya): The causal efficacy that transfers across parts of time for prayer obligation.
الجزء الأخير (al-juz' al-akhir): The last part of the prayer time when the obligation becomes established.
الاستيعاب والامتداد (al-isti'ab wa al-imtidad): Continuity and prolongation of insanity or unconsciousness exceeding a day and night, which drops the prayer obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how do the Hanafis resolve the conflict between the prohibition hadiths and the hadith 'Whoever catches a rak'ah before sunset has caught Asr'?
A) They accept the rak'ah hadith as superseding the prohibition
B) They resort to analogy (qiyas), which validates Asr but invalidates Fajr
C) They reject the rak'ah hadith as weak
D) They apply the prohibition to all prayers without exception

Key Takeaway
Conflicting hadiths are resolved by qiyas in Hanafi usul; for Asr, the rak'ah hadith is given effect, while for Fajr, the prohibition stands.

Expediting Zakah: The Hadith Proof
Narrating a hadith that permits expediting zakah before the year

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the hadith cited for expediting zakah, assess its authenticity (zanni), and apply the Hanafi principle that the year is a condition for completion (shart al-wujub al-mukammil), not for obligation.

Core Idea
The Prophet's permission to expedite zakah shows the year is not a condition for obligation, only for completion.

In this lesson, we examine a hadith reported from Ali that the Prophet allowed al-Abbas to pay his zakah before the year ended. This hadith is a key proof for the Hanafi ruling that expediting zakah is permissible. We will analyze its chain, its indication (dalala), and how it supports the underlying usul principle about the role of the year in zakah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its narrators
Find the core narration: Ali reported that al-Abbas asked the Prophet about expediting his sadaqah (zakah) before it was due, and the Prophet permitted it. Note the chain of narrators mentioned (the four except Nasa'i, plus Darimi, Ahmad, Abd al-Razzaq).
The hadith is ahad, not mutawatir.
2
Assess the chain's strength
Determine thubut: Since it is ahad, its transmission is zanni. This affects its use as evidence in Hanafi usul, but ahad hadith are still valid for establishing rulings.
Hanafis accept ahad hadith for non-essential matters or when supported by other evidence.
3
Analyze the legal indication (wajh al-dalalah)
The Prophet's permission (رخص) indicates that expediting is permissible. The key point: if the year were a condition for obligation (shart al-wujub), paying before the year would be invalid. The permission shows the year is not a condition for obligation, only for completion (shart al-wujub al-mukammil).
This is a classic Hanafi distinction.
4
Connect to Hanafi usul principle
The hadith supports the principle that the cause (sabab) of zakah is ownership of nisab, not the passing of the year. The year is a condition for full obligation but does not prevent early payment.
This principle has implications for other forms of ibadah with similar structures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجوز التعجيل: اعلم أنه قد ورد جواز تعجيل الصدقة (أي الزكاة) قبل تمام الحول في حديث علي الا الله أن العباس الله سأل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في تعجيل صدقته قبل أن تحل فرخص له في ذلك، رواه الأربعة إلا النسائي، وأخرجه الدارمي وأحمد و عبد الرزاق - له =
Expediting: know that the permissibility of expediting charity (i.e. zakah) before the completion of the year is reported in the hadith of Ali that al-Abbas asked the Prophet to expedite his charity before it was due and he permitted him in that. It is narrated by the four [sunan compilers] except al-Nasa'i, and also by al-Darimi, Ahmad, and Abd al-Razzaq.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage provides a hadith proof for the permissibility of paying zakah before the completion of the lunar year. The hadith involves Ali (or al-Abbas) asking the Prophet about expediting the zakah of al-Abbas, and the Prophet allowed it. This supports the earlier ruling that the cause of zakah is ownership of nisab, not the passing of the year.

Key Terms
التعجيل (al-ta'jil): Expediting the payment of zakah before the end of the lunar year.
شَرْطُ الْوُجُوبِ الْمُكَمِّلِ (shart al-wujub al-mukammil): A condition for complete obligation, not for the obligation itself. Missing it means the obligation is not fully due, but the action can still be performed early.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of the hadith cited in this passage?
A) To show that zakah is obligatory only after the year.
B) To prove that expediting zakah is permissible.
C) To prove that only al-Abbas could expedite.
D) To show that zakah can be delayed indefinitely.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of al-Abbas proves that expediting zakah is permissible, supporting the Hanafi view that the year is a condition for completion, not obligation.
